<p><b>Spain</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9a/En-us-Spain.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Spain.ogg" title="File:En-us-Spain.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="/eɪ/ long 'a' in 'base'">eɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>España</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[esˈpaɲa]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Es-Espa%C3%B1a.ogg" title="File:Es-España.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/64/Es-Espa%C3%B1a.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-España.ogg">listen</a>)</small>), officially the <b>Kingdom of Spain</b> (Spanish: <span lang="es"><i>Reino de España</i></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-a_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a-2">[a]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-b_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b-3">[b]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> located on the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">southwestern Europe</a>, with two large <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagos</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> off the North African Atlantic coast, two cities <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> in the North African mainland and several small islands in the <a href="/wiki/Alboran_Sea" title="Alboran Sea">Alboran Sea</a> near the Moroccan coast. <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Spain" title="Peninsular Spain">Its mainland</a> is bordered to the south and east by the Mediterranean Sea except for a small land boundary with <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a>; to the north and northeast by France, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a>; and to the west and northwest by Portugal and the Atlantic Ocean. It is the only European country to have a border with an African country (Morocco)<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[h]</a></sup> and its African territory accounts for nearly 5% of its population, mostly in the Canary Islands but also in Ceuta and Melilla.</p>
<p>With an area of 505,990&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (195,360&#160;sq&#160;mi), Spain is the largest country in Southern Europe, the second largest country in Western Europe and the European Union, and the <a href="/wiki/Area_and_population_of_European_countries" title="Area and population of European countries">fourth largest country in the European continent</a>. By population, Spain is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population" title="List of European countries by population">sixth</a> largest in Europe and the <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union#List" title="Member state of the European Union">fifth</a> in the European Union. Spain's capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>; other major <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Spain" title="List of metropolitan areas in Spain">urban areas</a> include <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">Málaga</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_humans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatomically modern humans">Modern humans</a> first arrived in the Iberian Peninsula around 35,000 years ago. <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberian</a> cultures along with ancient <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carthaginian_Iberia" title="Carthaginian Iberia">Carthaginian</a> settlements developed on the peninsula until it came under Roman rule around 200 BCE, after which the region was named <i><a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a></i>, based on the earlier Phoenician name <i>Span</i> or <i>Spania</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-historiaclasica.com_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historiaclasica.com-18">[10]</a></sup> In the Middle Ages, the area was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Germanic_tribes" class="mw-redirect" title="Germanic tribes">Germanic tribes</a> and later by the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>. Spain emerged as a unified country in the 15th century, following the marriage of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a> and the completion of the eight centuries-long reconquest, or <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i> from the Moors in 1492. In the early modern period, Spain became one of history's first <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">global colonial empires</a>, leaving a vast cultural and linguistic legacy that includes over 500 million <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">Spanish speakers</a>, making Spanish the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">second most spoken first language</a>, after Mandarin Chinese.</p>
<p>Spain is a democracy organised in the form of a parliamentary government under a constitutional <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">monarchy</a>. It is a <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a> and a major <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[11]</a></sup> with the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">fourteenth largest economy</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">sixteenth largest</a> by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (UN), the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU), the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> (CoE), the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a> (OEI), the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD), the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO) and many other international organisations.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>
<p>The origins of the Roman name <i><a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a></i>, from which the modern name <i>España</i> was derived, are uncertain due to inadequate evidence, although it is documented that the Phoenicians and Carthaginians referred to the region as <i>Spania</i>, therefore the most widely accepted etymology is a Semitic – Phoenician one.<sup id="cite_ref-historiaclasica.com_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historiaclasica.com-18">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[12]</a></sup> Down the centuries there have been a number of accounts and hypotheses:</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dama_de_Elche_(M.A.N._Madrid)_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Dama_de_Elche_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_01.jpg/170px-Dama_de_Elche_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_01.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Dama_de_Elche_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_01.jpg/255px-Dama_de_Elche_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Dama_de_Elche_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_01.jpg/340px-Dama_de_Elche_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="975" data-file-height="1224" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dama_de_Elche_(M.A.N._Madrid)_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Lady_of_Elche" title="Lady of Elche">Lady of Elche</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> scholar <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Nebrija" title="Antonio de Nebrija">Antonio de Nebrija</a> proposed that the word <i>Hispania</i> evolved from the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_language" title="Iberian language">Iberian</a> word <i><a href="/wiki/Hispalis" class="mw-redirect" title="Hispalis">Hispalis</a></i>, meaning "city of the western world".</p>
<p>Jesús Luis Cunchillos argues that the root of the term <i>span</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">Phoenician</a> word <i>spy</i>, meaning "to forge metals". Therefore, <i>i-spn-ya</i> would mean "the land where metals are forged".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[13]</a></sup> It may be a derivation of the Phoenician <i>I-Shpania</i>, meaning "island of rabbits", "land of rabbits" or "edge", a reference to Spain's location at the end of the Mediterranean; Roman coins struck in the region from the reign of <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a> show a female figure with a <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">rabbit</a> at her feet,<sup id="cite_ref-burke_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burke-22">[14]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> called it the "land of the rabbits".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Hispania</i> may derive from the poetic use of the term <i>Hesperia</i>, reflecting the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> perception of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> as a "western land" or "land of the setting sun" (<i>Hesperia</i>, <i>Ἑσπερία</i> in <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>) and Spain, being still further west, as <i>Hesperia ultima</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-anthon_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anthon-24">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is the claim that "Hispania" derives from the <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> word <i>Ezpanna</i> meaning "edge" or "border", another reference to the fact that the Iberian Peninsula constitutes the southwest corner of the European continent.<sup id="cite_ref-anthon_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anthon-24">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two 15th-century Spanish Jewish scholars, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Abravanel" title="Isaac Abravanel">Don Isaac Abravanel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solomon_ibn_Verga" title="Solomon ibn Verga">Solomon ibn Verga</a>, gave an explanation now considered folkloric. Both men wrote in two different published works that the first Jews to reach Spain were brought by ship by Phiros who was confederate with the king of Babylon when he laid siege to Jerusalem. This man was a <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Grecian</a> by birth, but who had been given a kingdom in Spain. He became related by marriage to Espan, the nephew of king Heracles, who also ruled over a kingdom in Spain. Heracles later renounced his throne in preference for his native Greece, leaving his kingdom to his nephew, Espan, from whom the country of <i>España</i> (Spain) took its name. Based upon their testimonies, this eponym would have already been in use in Spain by c. 350 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Spain" title="History of Spain">History of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AltamiraBison.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/AltamiraBison.jpg/220px-AltamiraBison.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/AltamiraBison.jpg/330px-AltamiraBison.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/AltamiraBison.jpg/440px-AltamiraBison.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2436" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AltamiraBison.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Reproduction of <a href="/wiki/Altamira_Cave" class="mw-redirect" title="Altamira Cave">Altamira Cave</a> paintings,<sup id="cite_ref-Science2012_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Science2012-26">[18]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">Cantabria</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Iberia enters written records as a land populated largely by the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>. Early on its coastal areas were settled by <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> who founded Western Europe´s most ancient cities <a href="/wiki/Cadiz" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadiz">Cadiz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaga" class="mw-redirect" title="Malaga">Malaga</a>. Phoenician influence expanded as much of the Peninsula was eventually incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Carthaginian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginian Empire">Carthaginian Empire</a>, becoming a major theater of the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a> against the expanding <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. After an <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Roman conquest of Hispania">arduous conquest</a>, the peninsula came fully under Roman Rule. During the early Middle Ages it came under Germanic rule but later, much of it was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Moorish" class="mw-redirect" title="Moorish">Moorish</a> invaders from North Africa. In a process that took centuries, the small Christian kingdoms in the north gradually regained control of the peninsula. The last Moorish kingdom fell in the same year Columbus reached the Americas. A global empire began which saw Spain become the strongest kingdom in Europe, the leading world power for a century and a half, and the largest overseas empire for three centuries.</p>
<p>Continued wars and other problems eventually led to a diminished status. The Napoleonic invasions of Spain led to chaos, triggering independence movements that tore apart most of the empire and left the country politically unstable. Prior to the Second World War, Spain suffered a devastating civil war and came under the rule of an authoritarian government, which oversaw a period of stagnation that was followed by a surge in the growth of the economy. Eventually democracy was peacefully restored in the form of a parliamentary constitutional monarchy. Spain joined the European Union, experiencing a cultural renaissance and steady economic growth.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_pre-Roman_peoples">Prehistory and pre-Roman peoples</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Iberia" title="Prehistoric Iberia">Prehistoric Iberia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg/220px-2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg/330px-2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg/440px-2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5225" data-file-height="3483" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_Castro_de_Santa_Trega._Galiza-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Castro_culture" title="Castro culture">castro</a> in <a href="/wiki/A_Guarda" title="A Guarda">A Guarda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galicia,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Galicia, Spain">Galicia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Archaeological research at <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_Site_of_Atapuerca" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological Site of Atapuerca">Atapuerca</a> indicates the Iberian Peninsula was populated by <a href="/wiki/Hominid" class="mw-redirect" title="Hominid">hominids</a> 1.2&#160;million years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[19]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Atapuerca_Mountains" title="Atapuerca Mountains">Atapuerca</a> fossils have been found of the earliest known <a href="/wiki/Hominins" class="mw-redirect" title="Hominins">hominins</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Homo_antecessor" title="Homo antecessor">Homo antecessor</a>. Modern humans first arrived in Iberia, from the north on foot, about 35,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[20]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2016)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> The best known artefacts of these prehistoric human settlements are the famous paintings in the <a href="/wiki/Altamira_(cave)" class="mw-redirect" title="Altamira (cave)">Altamira cave</a> of Cantabria in northern Iberia, which were created from 35,600 to 13,500 <a href="/wiki/Before_Common_Era" class="mw-redirect" title="Before Common Era">BCE</a> by <a href="/wiki/Cro-Magnon" title="Cro-Magnon">Cro-Magnon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Science2012_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Science2012-26">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[21]</a></sup> Archaeological and genetic evidence suggests that the Iberian Peninsula acted as one of several major refugia from which northern Europe was repopulated following the end of the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">last ice age</a>.</p>
<p>The largest groups inhabiting the Iberian Peninsula before the Roman conquest were the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>. The Iberians inhabited the Mediterranean side of the peninsula, from the northeast to the southeast. The Celts inhabited much of the inner and Atlantic sides of the peninsula, from the northwest to the southwest. <a href="/wiki/Basque_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque people">Basques</a> occupied the western area of the Pyrenees mountain range and adjacent areas, the Phoenician-influenced <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">Tartessians</a> culture flourished in the southwest and the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vettones" title="Vettones">Vettones</a> occupied areas in the central west. A number of cities were founded along the coast by <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, and trading outposts were established by <a href="/wiki/Greek_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek colonies">Greeks</a> in the North East. Eventually, Phoenician-<a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a> expanded inland conquering about over half of modern-day Spain.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Empire_and_the_Gothic_Kingdom">Roman Empire and the Gothic Kingdom</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_(4).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_%284%29.JPG/220px-Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_%284%29.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_%284%29.JPG/330px-Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_%284%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_%284%29.JPG/440px-Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_%284%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2352" data-file-height="1568" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teatro_Romano_de_M%C3%A9rida_(4).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Roman_Theatre_(M%C3%A9rida)" title="Roman Theatre (Mérida)">Roman Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9rida,_Spain" title="Mérida, Spain">Mérida</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a>, an expanding <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> captured Carthaginian trading colonies along the Mediterranean coast from roughly 210 to 205&#160;BC. It took the Romans nearly two centuries to complete the conquest of the Iberian Peninsula, though they had control of it for over six centuries. Roman rule was bound together by law, language, and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_road" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman road">Roman road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hispania_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hispania-30">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n,_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain,_Senate_Palace,_Madrid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n%2C_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain%2C_Senate_Palace%2C_Madrid.jpg/220px-Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n%2C_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain%2C_Senate_Palace%2C_Madrid.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n%2C_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain%2C_Senate_Palace%2C_Madrid.jpg/330px-Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n%2C_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain%2C_Senate_Palace%2C_Madrid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n%2C_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain%2C_Senate_Palace%2C_Madrid.jpg/440px-Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n%2C_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain%2C_Senate_Palace%2C_Madrid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="2334" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reccared_I_Conversi%C3%B3n,_by_Mu%C3%B1oz_Degrain,_Senate_Palace,_Madrid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Conversion of <a href="/wiki/Reccared" class="mw-redirect" title="Reccared">Reccared</a> to <a href="/wiki/Chalcedonian_Christianity" title="Chalcedonian Christianity">Chalcedonian Christianity</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The cultures of the Celtic and Iberian populations were gradually <a href="/wiki/Romanisation_(cultural)" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanisation (cultural)">Romanised</a> (Latinised) at differing rates in different parts of <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">Hispania</a>. Local leaders were admitted into the Roman aristocratic class.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[i]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-country_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country-32">[23]</a></sup> Hispania served as a granary for the Roman market, and its harbours exported <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>. Agricultural production increased with the introduction of irrigation projects, some of which remain in use. Emperors <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">Theodosius I</a>, and the philosopher <a href="/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger" title="Seneca the Younger">Seneca</a> were born in Hispania.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[j]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> was introduced into Hispania in the 1st century AD and it became popular in the cities in the 2nd century AD.<sup id="cite_ref-country_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-country-32">[23]</a></sup> Most of Spain's present languages and religion, and the basis of its laws, originate from this period.<sup id="cite_ref-hispania_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hispania-30">[22]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo,_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg/170px-Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg/255px-Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg/340px-Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo%2C_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1868" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alcazar_of_Toledo_-_Toledo,_Spain_-_Dec_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a>, capital of the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The weakening of the Western Roman Empire's jurisdiction in Hispania began in 409, when the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, together with the <a href="/wiki/Sarmatian" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarmatian">Sarmatian</a> <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, crossed the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> and ravaged <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> drove them into Iberia that same year. The Suebi established a kingdom in what is today modern <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> whereas the Vandals briefly established themselves in southern Spain before crossing over to North Africa and conquering Carthage. As the western empire disintegrated, the social and economic base became greatly simplified: but even in modified form, the successor regimes maintained many of the institutions and laws of the late empire, including Christianity and assimilation to the evolving Roman culture.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantines</a> established an enclave, <a href="/wiki/Spania" title="Spania">Spania</a>, in the south, with the intention of reviving the Roman empire throughout Iberia. Eventually, however, Hispania was reunited under <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic rule</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Isidore_of_Seville" title="Isidore of Seville">Isidore of Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">archbishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, was an influential philosopher and was much studied in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. Also, his theories were vital to the conversion of the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a> to a Catholic one, in the <a href="/wiki/Councils_of_Toledo" title="Councils of Toledo">Councils of Toledo</a>. This <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Gothic</a> kingdom was the first Christian kingdom ruling in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a> it was the referent for the different kingdoms fighting against the Muslim rule.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages:_Muslim_era_and_Reconquista">Middle Ages: Muslim era and Reconquista</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mort_de_Roland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mort_de_Roland.jpg/220px-Mort_de_Roland.jpg" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mort_de_Roland.jpg/330px-Mort_de_Roland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Mort_de_Roland.jpg/440px-Mort_de_Roland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="493" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mort_de_Roland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The death of the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Roland" title="Roland">Roland</a> defeated by a <a href="/wiki/Basque_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque people">Basque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a>-<a href="/wiki/Muladi" title="Muladi">Muladi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Banu_Qasi" title="Banu Qasi">Banu Qasi</a>) alliance at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Roncevaux_Pass_(778)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Roncevaux Pass (778)">Battle of Roncevaux Pass (778)</a> originated the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Kingdom of Navarre</a> led by <a href="/wiki/%C3%8D%C3%B1igo_Arista_of_Pamplona" title="Íñigo Arista of Pamplona">Íñigo Arista</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 8th century, nearly all of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> was <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">conquered</a> (711–718) by largely <a href="/wiki/Moorish" class="mw-redirect" title="Moorish">Moorish</a> <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> armies from North Africa. These conquests were part of the expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a>. Only a small area in the mountainous north-west of the peninsula managed to resist the initial invasion.</p>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Islamic law</a>, Christians and <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a> were given the subordinate status of <a href="/wiki/Dhimmi" title="Dhimmi">dhimmi</a>. This status permitted Christians and Jews to practice their religions as <i><a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Book" title="People of the Book">People of the Book</a></i> but they were required to pay a special tax and had legal and social rights inferior to those of Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Conversion to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> proceeded at an increasing pace. The <i><a href="/wiki/Muladi" title="Muladi">muladíes</a></i> (Muslims of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian</a> origin) are believed to have comprised the majority of the population of Al-Andalus by the end of the 10th century.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chap2_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chap2-37">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Muslim community in the Iberian Peninsula was itself diverse and beset by social tensions. The <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berber people</a> of North Africa, who had provided the bulk of the invading armies, <a href="/wiki/Berber_Revolt" title="Berber Revolt">clashed with the Arab leadership</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[k]</a></sup> Over time, large Moorish populations became established, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Guadalquivir River">Guadalquivir River</a> valley, the coastal plain of <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ebro_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebro River">Ebro River</a> valley and (towards the end of this period) in the mountainous region of <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-chap2_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chap2-37">[27]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg/220px-Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg/330px-Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg/440px-Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3762" data-file-height="2235" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spain_Andalusia_Cordoba_BW_2015-10-27_13-54-14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hypostyle hall in the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral%E2%80%93Mosque_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral–Mosque of Córdoba">Great Mosque of Córdoba</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Córdoba, Spain">Córdoba</a>, the capital of the caliphate since <a href="/wiki/Abd-ar-Rahman_III" title="Abd-ar-Rahman III">Abd-ar-Rahman III</a>, was the largest, richest and most sophisticated city in western Europe. Mediterranean trade and cultural exchange flourished. Muslims imported a rich intellectual tradition from the Middle East and North Africa. Muslim and Jewish scholars played an important part in reviving and expanding classical <a href="/wiki/Greek_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek culture">Greek learning</a> in Western Europe. Some important philosophers at the time were <a href="/wiki/Averroes" title="Averroes">Averroes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Arabi" title="Ibn Arabi">Ibn Arabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maimonides" title="Maimonides">Maimonides</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Romanisation_(cultural)" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanisation (cultural)">Romanised</a> cultures of the Iberian Peninsula interacted with Muslim and Jewish cultures in complex ways, giving the region a distinctive culture.<sup id="cite_ref-chap2_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chap2-37">[27]</a></sup> Outside the cities, where the vast majority lived, the land ownership system from Roman times remained largely intact as Muslim leaders rarely dispossessed landowners and the introduction of new crops and techniques led to an expansion of agriculture.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg/170px-Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg" width="170" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg/255px-Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg/340px-Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="772" data-file-height="856" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Petronilla_of_Aragon" title="Petronilla of Aragon">Petronilla of Aragon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Berenguer_IV,_Count_of_Barcelona" title="Ramon Berenguer IV, Count of Barcelona">Ramon Berenguer IV, Count of Barcelona</a>, dynastic union of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 11th century, the Muslim holdings fractured into rival <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">Taifa</a> kingdoms, allowing the small Christian states the opportunity to greatly enlarge their territories.<sup id="cite_ref-chap2_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chap2-37">[27]</a></sup> The arrival from <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> of the Islamic ruling sects of the <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Almohads" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> restored unity upon the Muslim holdings, with a stricter, less tolerant application of Islam, and saw a revival in Muslim fortunes. This re-united Islamic state experienced more than a century of successes that partially reversed Christian gains.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg/220px-Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg/330px-Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg/440px-Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="544" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pante%C3%B3nSanIsidoroLe%C3%B3n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Isidoro" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of San Isidoro">Basilica of San Isidoro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="León (Spain)">León</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i> (Reconquest) was the centuries-long period in which Christian rule was re-established over the Iberian Peninsula. The Reconquista is viewed as beginning with the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Covadonga" title="Battle of Covadonga">Battle of Covadonga</a> won by <a href="/wiki/Pelagius_of_Asturias" title="Pelagius of Asturias">Don Pelayo</a> in 722 and was concurrent with the period of Muslim rule on the Iberian Peninsula. The Christian army's victory over Muslim forces led to the creation of the Christian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a> along the northwestern coastal mountains. Shortly after, in 739, Muslim forces were driven from <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>, which was to eventually host one of medieval Europe's holiest sites, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Compostela" title="Santiago de Compostela">Santiago de Compostela</a> and was incorporated into the new Christian kingdom. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of León">Kingdom of León</a> was the strongest Christian kingdom for centuries. In 1188 the first modern parliamentary session in Europe was held in <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="León (Spain)">León</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cortes_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Cortes of León">Cortes of León</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a>, formed from Leonese territory, was its successor as strongest kingdom. The kings and the nobility fought for power and influence in this period. The example of the Roman emperors influenced the political objective of the Crown, while the nobles benefited from <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>.</p>
<p>Muslim armies had also moved north of the Pyrenees but they were defeated by Frankish forces at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tours" title="Battle of Tours">Battle of Poitiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francia" title="Francia">Frankia</a>. Later, <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> forces established <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">Christian counties</a> on the southern side of the Pyrenees. These areas were to grow into the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Aragon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[28]</a></sup> For several centuries, the fluctuating frontier between the Muslim and Christian controlled areas of Iberia was along the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> valleys.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ramon_Llull.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ramon_Llull.jpg/150px-Ramon_Llull.jpg" width="150" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ramon_Llull.jpg/225px-Ramon_Llull.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Ramon_Llull.jpg/300px-Ramon_Llull.jpg 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="1084" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ramon_Llull.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ramon_Llull" title="Ramon Llull">Ramon Llull</a>, prominent <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Friars_Minor" title="Order of Friars Minor">Franciscan</a> philosopher of <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mysticism" title="Mysticism">mysticism</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/County_of_Barcelona" title="County of Barcelona">County of Barcelona</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Kingdom of Aragon</a> entered in a dynastic union and gained territory and power in the Mediterranean. In 1229 <a href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a> was conquered, so was <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> in 1238.</p>
<p>The break-up of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a> into the competing taifa kingdoms helped the long embattled Iberian Christian kingdoms gain the initiative. The capture of the strategically central city of <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a> in 1085 marked a significant shift in the balance of power in favour of the Christian kingdoms. Following a great Muslim resurgence in the 12th century, the great Moorish strongholds in the south fell to Christian Spain in the 13th century—Córdoba in 1236 and <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a> in 1248. After 800 years of Muslim presence in Spain, the last Nasrid sultanate of <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tributary_(political)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tributary (political)">tributary state</a> would finally surrender in 1492 to the Catholic monarchs <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Queen Isabella I</a> of <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[29]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">King Ferdinand II</a> of <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Arag%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown of Aragón">Aragon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[32]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg/220px-LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg/330px-LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg/440px-LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1447" data-file-height="864" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LibroDesJuegasAlfonXAndCourt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfonso X">Alfonso X</a>, pretendant of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> crown and king of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Crown of Castile</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From the mid 13th century, literature and philosophy started to flourish again in the Christian peninsular kingdoms, based on Roman and Gothic traditions. An important philosopher from this time is <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Llull" title="Ramon Llull">Ramon Llull</a>. <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Cresques" title="Abraham Cresques">Abraham Cresques</a> was a prominent Jewish cartographer. <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a> and its institutions were the model for the legislators. The king <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X_of_Castile" title="Alfonso X of Castile">Alfonso X of Castile</a> focused on strengthening this Roman and Gothic past, and also on linking the Iberian Christian kingdoms with the rest of medieval European Christendom. He worked for being elected emperor of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and published the <a href="/wiki/Siete_Partidas" title="Siete Partidas">Siete Partidas</a> code. The <a href="/wiki/Toledo_School_of_Translators" title="Toledo School of Translators">Toledo School of Translators</a> is the name that commonly describes the group of scholars who worked together in the city of Toledo during the 12th and 13th centuries, to translate many of the philosophical and scientific works from <a href="/wiki/Classical_Arabic" title="Classical Arabic">Classical Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Hebrew" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Hebrew">Ancient Hebrew</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Transmission_of_the_Classics" class="mw-redirect" title="Transmission of the Classics">Islamic transmission of the classics</a> is the main <a href="/wiki/Islamic_contributions_to_Medieval_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic contributions to Medieval Europe">Islamic contributions to Medieval Europe</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Spanish">Castilian</a> language—more commonly known (especially later in history and at present) as "Spanish" after becoming the national language and <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i> of Spain—evolved from <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a>, as did other <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a> of Spain like the <a href="/wiki/Old_Catalan" title="Old Catalan">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese" class="mw-redirect" title="Astur-Leonese">Asturian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician</a> languages, as well as other Romance languages in Latin Europe. <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>, the only non-Romance language in Spain, continued evolving from Early Basque to Medieval. The <a href="/wiki/Glosas_Emilianenses" title="Glosas Emilianenses">Glosas Emilianenses</a> founded in the <a href="/wiki/Monasteries_of_San_Mill%C3%A1n_de_la_Cogolla" title="Monasteries of San Millán de la Cogolla">monasteries</a> of <a href="/wiki/San_Mill%C3%A1n_de_la_Cogolla" title="San Millán de la Cogolla">San Millán de la Cogolla</a> contain the first written words in both Basque and Spanish, having the first become an influence in the formation of the second as an evolution of Latin.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg/220px-Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg/330px-Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg/440px-Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3931" data-file-height="2595" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alhambra_L%C3%B6wenhof_mit_L%C3%B6wenbrunnen_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alhambra" title="Alhambra">Alhambra</a>. Granada was the last <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">Taifa</a> in the Peninsula.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 13th and 14th centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Marinid" class="mw-redirect" title="Marinid">Marinid</a> Muslim sect based in North Africa invaded and established some enclaves on the southern coast but failed in their attempt to re-establish Muslim rule in Iberia and were soon driven out. The 13th century also witnessed the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>, centred in Spain's north east, expand its reach across islands in the Mediterranean, to <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> and even Athens.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[33]</a></sup> Around this time the universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Palencia" title="University of Palencia">Palencia</a> (1212/1263) and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Salamanca" title="University of Salamanca">Salamanca</a> (1218/1254) were established. The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> of 1348 and 1349 devastated Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Spain">Imperial Spain</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg/220px-University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg/330px-University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg/440px-University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1537" data-file-height="1153" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Salamanca_Fray_Luis_de_Leon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Salamanca" title="Salamanca">Salamanca</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Sites">UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a>. The <a href="/wiki/School_of_Salamanca" title="School of Salamanca">School of Salamanca</a> was the intellectual origin of modern <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1469, the crowns of the Christian kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Aragon</a> were united by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">marriage</a> of <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand II of Aragon</a>. 1478 commenced the completion of the conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> and in 1492, the combined forces of Castile and Aragon captured the Emirate of Granada, ending the last remnant of a <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Muslim_presence_in_the_Iberian_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of the Muslim presence in the Iberian peninsula">781-year presence</a> of Islamic rule in Iberia. That same year, <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Spain's Jews</a> were <a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">ordered to convert</a> to <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholicism</a> or face <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">expulsion</a> from Spanish territories during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[35]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Granada">Treaty of Granada</a> guaranteed religious tolerance towards Muslims,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[36]</a></sup> and although the tolerance was only partial, it was not until the beginning of the 17th century, following the <a href="/wiki/Morisco_rebellions_in_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="Morisco rebellions in Granada">Revolt of the Alpujarras</a>, that Muslims were finally expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[l]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cong_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cong-49">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The year 1492 also marked the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, during a voyage funded by Isabella. Columbus's first voyage crossed the Atlantic and reached the Caribbean Islands, beginning the European exploration and conquest of the Americas, although he remained convinced that he had reached the <a href="/wiki/Orient" title="Orient">Orient</a>. The colonisation of the Americas started, with <i><a href="/wiki/Conquistador" title="Conquistador">conquistadores</a></i> like <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pizarro" title="Francisco Pizarro">Francisco Pizarro</a>. <a href="/wiki/Miscegenation" title="Miscegenation">Miscegenation</a> was the rule between the native and the European cultures and people.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG/220px-Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG/330px-Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG/440px-Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1147" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emanuel_Gottlieb_Leutze_-_Columbus_Before_the_Queen.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> meets <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand II of Aragon</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Alhambra" title="Alhambra">Alhambra</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> <a href="/wiki/New_Monarchs" title="New Monarchs">New Monarchs</a>, Isabella and Ferdinand centralised royal power at the expense of local nobility, and the word <i>España</i>, whose root is the ancient name <i>Hispania</i>, began to be commonly used to designate the whole of the two kingdoms.<sup id="cite_ref-cong_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cong-49">[37]</a></sup> With their wide-ranging political, legal, religious and military reforms, Spain emerged as the first <a href="/wiki/Historical_powers#Spanish_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical powers">world power</a>.</p>
<p>The unification of the crowns of Aragon and Castile by the marriage of their sovereigns laid the basis for modern Spain and the Spanish Empire, although each kingdom of Spain remained a separate country, in social, political, laws, currency and language.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[39]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg/220px-Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg.png" width="220" height="113" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg/330px-Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg/440px-Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="443" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Imperio_Espa%C3%B1ol_Completo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Anachronous map of the Spanish Empire including territorial claims.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There were two big revolts against the new Habsburg monarch and the more authoritarian and imperial-style crown: <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Comuneros" title="Revolt of the Comuneros">Revolt of the Comuneros</a> in <a href="/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)" title="Castile (historical region)">Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Brotherhoods" title="Revolt of the Brotherhoods">Revolt of the Brotherhoods</a> in <a href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">Majorca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>. After years of combat, Comuneros <a href="/wiki/Juan_L%C3%B3pez_de_Padilla" title="Juan López de Padilla">Juan López de Padilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bravo" title="Juan Bravo">Juan Bravo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Maldonado" title="Francisco Maldonado">Francisco Maldonado</a> were executed and <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Pacheco" title="María Pacheco">María Pacheco</a> went into exile. <a href="/wiki/Germaine_of_Foix" title="Germaine of Foix">Germana de Foix</a> also finished with the revolt in the Mediterranean.</p>
<p>Spain was Europe's leading power throughout the 16th century and most of the 17th century, a position reinforced by trade and wealth from colonial possessions and became the world's leading <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">maritime power</a>. It reached its apogee during the reigns of the first two <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Spanish Habsburgs</a>—<a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles I of Spain">Charles I</a> (1516–1556) and <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a> (1556–1598). This period saw the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Wars" title="Italian Wars">Italian Wars</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Comuneros" title="Revolt of the Comuneros">Revolt of the Comuneros</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Revolt" title="Dutch Revolt">Dutch Revolt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Morisco_rebellions_in_Granada" class="mw-redirect" title="Morisco rebellions in Granada">Morisco Revolt</a>, clashes with the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman-Habsburg_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman-Habsburg wars">Ottomans</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1585%E2%80%931604)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1585–1604)">Anglo-Spanish War</a> and wars with <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_France#The_French_Renaissance" title="Early modern France">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Through exploration and conquest or royal marriage alliances and inheritance, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> expanded to include vast areas in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, islands in the Asia-Pacific area, areas of Italy, cities in Northern Africa, as well as parts of what are now France, Germany, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Magellan%27s_circumnavigation" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Magellan's circumnavigation">first circumnavigation</a> of the world was carried out in 1519–1521. It was the first empire on which it was said that <a href="/wiki/The_empire_on_which_the_sun_never_sets" title="The empire on which the sun never sets">the sun never set</a>. This was an <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, with daring explorations by sea and by land, the opening-up of new <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">trade routes</a> across oceans, conquests and the beginnings of European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a>. Spanish explorers brought back <a href="/wiki/Precious_metal" title="Precious metal">precious metals</a>, spices, luxuries, and previously unknown plants, and played a leading part in transforming the European understanding of the globe.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[41]</a></sup> The cultural efflorescence witnessed during this period is now referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Golden_Age" title="Spanish Golden Age">Spanish Golden Age</a>. The expansion of the empire caused immense upheaval in the Americas as the collapse of societies and empires and new diseases from Europe devastated American indigenous populations. The rise of <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanism</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a> and new geographical discoveries and conquests raised issues that were addressed by the intellectual movement now known as the <a href="/wiki/School_of_Salamanca" title="School of Salamanca">School of Salamanca</a>, which developed the first modern theories of what are now known as <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:314px;max-width:314px">
