</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:158px;max-width:158px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg,_by_Titian,_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/156px-Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" width="156" height="185" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/234px-Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/312px-Carlos_V_en_M%C3%BChlberg%2C_by_Titian%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="25284" data-file-height="30000" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Habsburg Spain</a>. Charles was also Emperor of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the late 16th century and first half of the 17th century, Spain was confronted by unrelenting challenges from all sides. <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a>, under the aegis of the rapidly growing <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, disrupted life in many coastal areas through their <a href="/wiki/Slave" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave">slave</a> raids and the renewed threat of an <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim conquests">Islamic invasion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[42]</a></sup> This was at a time when Spain was often at war with France.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> dragged the kingdom ever more deeply into the mire of religiously charged wars. The result was a country forced into ever expanding military efforts across Europe and in the Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the middle decades of a war- and <a href="/wiki/Great_Plague_of_Seville" title="Great Plague of Seville">plague</a>-ridden 17th-century Europe, the Spanish Habsburgs had enmeshed the country in continent-wide religious-political conflicts. These conflicts drained it of resources and undermined the economy generally. Spain managed to hold on to most of the scattered <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg empire">Habsburg empire</a>, and help the imperial forces of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> reverse a large part of the advances made by Protestant forces, but it was finally forced to recognise the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">separation of Portugal</a> (with whom it had been <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">united</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> of the crowns from 1580 to 1640) and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, and eventually suffered some serious military reverses to France in the latter stages of the immensely destructive, Europe-wide <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[44]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_familia_de_Felipe_V_(Van_Loo).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/220px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/330px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg/440px-La_familia_de_Felipe_V_%28Van_Loo%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2717" data-file-height="2161" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_familia_de_Felipe_V_(Van_Loo).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/The_Family_of_Philip_V_(1743)" title="The Family of Philip V (1743)">The Family of Philip V (1743)</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Spain" title="Enlightenment in Spain">Enlightenment in Spain</a> a new royal family reigned, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">House of Bourbon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the latter half of the 17th century, Spain went into a gradual decline, during which it surrendered several small territories to France and the Netherlands; however, it maintained and enlarged its vast overseas empire, which remained intact until the beginning of the 19th century.</p>
<p>The decline culminated in a controversy over succession to the throne which consumed the first years of the 18th century. The <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> was a wide-ranging international conflict combined with a civil war, and was to cost the kingdom its European possessions and its position as one of the leading powers on the Continent.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[45]</a></sup> During this war, a new dynasty originating in France, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbons</a>, was installed. Long united only by the Crown, a true Spanish state was established when the first Bourbon king, <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V</a>, united the crowns of Castile and Aragon into a single state, abolishing many of the old regional privileges and laws.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 18th century saw a gradual recovery and an increase in prosperity through much of the empire. The new Bourbon monarchy drew on the French system of modernising the administration and the economy. <a href="/wiki/Enlightenment_in_Spain" title="Enlightenment in Spain">Enlightenment</a> ideas began to gain ground among some of the kingdom's elite and monarchy. Military assistance for the rebellious British colonies in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a> improved the kingdom's international standing.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberalism_and_nation_state">Liberalism and nation state</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mid-19th-century_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Mid-19th-century Spain">Mid-19th-century Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism_in_Spain" title="Anarchism in Spain">Anarchism in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Tres_de_Mayo,_by_Francisco_de_Goya,_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/El_Tres_de_Mayo%2C_by_Francisco_de_Goya%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/220px-El_Tres_de_Mayo%2C_by_Francisco_de_Goya%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/El_Tres_de_Mayo%2C_by_Francisco_de_Goya%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/330px-El_Tres_de_Mayo%2C_by_Francisco_de_Goya%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/El_Tres_de_Mayo%2C_by_Francisco_de_Goya%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/440px-El_Tres_de_Mayo%2C_by_Francisco_de_Goya%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="30000" data-file-height="23131" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Tres_de_Mayo,_by_Francisco_de_Goya,_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/The_Third_of_May_1808" title="The Third of May 1808">The Third of May 1808</a> by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Goya" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco de Goya">Francisco de Goya</a> depicts an episode of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Spanish Independence War</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1793, Spain went to war against the revolutionary new <a href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="First French Republic">French Republic</a> as a member of <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_First_Coalition" title="War of the First Coalition">the first Coalition</a>. The subsequent <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pyrenees" title="War of the Pyrenees">War of the Pyrenees</a> polarised the country in a reaction against the <a href="/wiki/Francization" title="Francization">gallicised</a> elites and following defeat in the field, peace was made with France in 1795 at the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Basel" title="Peace of Basel">Peace of Basel</a> in which Spain lost control over two-thirds of the island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>. The Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Godoy,_Prince_of_the_Peace" class="mw-redirect" title="Manuel Godoy, Prince of the Peace">Manuel Godoy</a>, then ensured that Spain allied herself with France in the brief <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Third_Coalition" title="War of the Third Coalition">War of the Third Coalition</a> which ended with the British victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a> in 1805. In 1807, a secret treaty between Napoleon and the unpopular prime minister led to a new declaration of war against Britain and Portugal. Napoleon's troops entered the country to invade Portugal but instead occupied Spain's major fortresses. The ridiculed Spanish king abdicated in favour of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon's</a> brother, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph Bonaparte</a>.</p>
<p>Joseph Bonaparte was seen as a <a href="/wiki/Puppet_monarch" title="Puppet monarch">puppet monarch</a> and was regarded with scorn by the Spanish. The <a href="/wiki/Dos_de_Mayo_Uprising" title="Dos de Mayo Uprising">2 May 1808 revolt</a> was one of many nationalist uprisings across the country against the Bonapartist regime.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[48]</a></sup> These revolts marked the beginning of a devastating <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">war of independence</a> against the Napoleonic regime.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[49]</a></sup> Napoleon was forced to intervene personally, defeating several Spanish armies and forcing a British army to retreat. However, further military action by Spanish armies, <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guerrilla">guerrillas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Wellington's</a> British-Portuguese forces, combined with Napoleon's disastrous <a href="/wiki/Napoleon%27s_Invasion_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon's Invasion of Russia">invasion of Russia</a>, led to the ousting of the French imperial armies from Spain in 1814, and the return of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">King Ferdinand VII</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the war, in 1810, a revolutionary body, the <a href="/wiki/Cortes_of_C%C3%A1diz" class="mw-redirect" title="Cortes of Cádiz">Cortes of Cádiz</a>, was assembled to co-ordinate the effort against the Bonapartist regime and to prepare a constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[51]</a></sup> It met as one body, and its members represented the entire Spanish empire.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[52]</a></sup> In 1812 a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1812" title="Spanish Constitution of 1812">constitution</a> for universal representation under a constitutional monarchy was declared but after the fall of the Bonapartist regime <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand VII">Ferdinand VII</a> dismissed the <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Cortes Generales</a> and was determined to rule as an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarch</a>. These events foreshadowed the conflict between conservatives and liberals in the 19th and early 20th centuries.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg/220px-Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg/330px-Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg/440px-Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2917" data-file-height="1612" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cortes_de_cadiz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1812" title="Spanish Constitution of 1812">Spanish Constitution of 1812</a> in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spain's conquest by France benefited Latin American anti-colonialists who resented the Imperial Spanish government's policies that favoured Spanish-born citizens (<a href="/wiki/Peninsulars" title="Peninsulars">Peninsulars</a>) over those born overseas (<a href="/wiki/Criollo_people" title="Criollo people">Criollos</a>) and demanded <a href="/wiki/Retroversion_of_the_sovereignty_to_the_people" title="Retroversion of the sovereignty to the people">retroversion of the sovereignty to the people</a>. Starting in 1809 Spain's American colonies began a series of revolutions and declared independence, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">Spanish American wars of independence</a> that ended Spanish control over its mainland colonies in the Americas. King Ferdinand VII's attempt to <a href="/wiki/Reconquista_(Spanish_America)" title="Reconquista (Spanish America)">re-assert control</a> proved futile as he faced opposition not only in the colonies but also in Spain and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain#Revolt" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">army revolts</a> followed, led by liberal officers. By the end of 1826, the only American colonies Spain held were <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>.</p>
<p>The Napoleonic War left Spain economically ruined, deeply divided and politically unstable. In the 1830s and 1840s Anti-liberal forces known as <a href="/wiki/Carlism" title="Carlism">Carlists</a> fought against <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Carlist_Wars" title="Carlist Wars">Carlist Wars</a>. Liberal forces won, but the conflict between progressive and conservative liberals ended in a weak early constitutional period. After the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution_(Spain)" title="Glorious Revolution (Spain)">Glorious Revolution</a> of 1868 and the short-lived <a href="/wiki/First_Spanish_Republic" title="First Spanish Republic">First Spanish Republic</a>, a more stable <a href="/wiki/Restoration_(Spain)" title="Restoration (Spain)">monarchic period began</a> characterised by the practice of <i>turnismo</i> (the rotation of government control between progressive and conservative liberals within the Spanish government).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barcelona,_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica,_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero,_de_Pellicer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Barcelona%2C_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica%2C_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero%2C_de_Pellicer.jpg/220px-Barcelona%2C_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica%2C_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero%2C_de_Pellicer.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Barcelona%2C_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica%2C_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero%2C_de_Pellicer.jpg/330px-Barcelona%2C_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica%2C_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero%2C_de_Pellicer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Barcelona%2C_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica%2C_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero%2C_de_Pellicer.jpg/440px-Barcelona%2C_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica%2C_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero%2C_de_Pellicer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1780" data-file-height="1320" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barcelona,_proclamaci%C3%B3n_de_la_rep%C3%BAblica,_aspecto_de_la_plaza_de_San_Jaime_en_la_ma%C3%B1ana_del_21_de_febrero,_de_Pellicer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/First_Spanish_Republic" title="First Spanish Republic">First Spanish Republic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, 1873. <a href="/wiki/Francesc_Pi_i_Margall" title="Francesc Pi i Margall">Francesc Pi i Margall</a>, was president and intellectual theoric of <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federalism</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the late 19th century nationalist movements arose in the Philippines and Cuba. In 1895 and 1896 the <a href="/wiki/Cuban_War_of_Independence" title="Cuban War of Independence">Cuban War of Independence</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolution" title="Philippine Revolution">Philippine Revolution</a> broke out and eventually the United States became involved. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> was fought in the spring of 1898 and resulted in Spain losing the last of its once vast colonial empire outside of North Africa. <i>El Desastre</i> (the Disaster), as the war became known in Spain, gave added impetus to the <a href="/wiki/Generation_of_%2798" title="Generation of '98">Generation of '98</a> who were conducting an analysis of the country.</p>
<p>Although the period around the turn of the century was one of increasing prosperity, the 20th century brought little peace; Spain played a minor part in the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">scramble for Africa</a>, with the colonisation of <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Morocco">Spanish Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>. It remained neutral during World War I (see <a href="/wiki/Spain_in_World_War_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Spain in World War I">Spain in World War I</a>). The heavy losses suffered during the <a href="/wiki/Rif_War_(1920)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rif War (1920)">Rif War</a> in Morocco brought discredit to the government and undermined the monarchy.</p>
<p>A period of authoritarian rule under General <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Primo_de_Rivera" title="Miguel Primo de Rivera">Miguel Primo de Rivera</a> (1923–1931) ended with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a>. The Republic offered political autonomy to the linguistically distinct regions of <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and gave <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage#Spain" title="Women's suffrage">voting rights to women</a>. <a href="/wiki/Clara_Campoamor" title="Clara Campoamor">Clara Campoamor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Suffragette" title="Suffragette">suffragette</a> leader), <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Kent" title="Victoria Kent">Victoria Kent</a> or <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Ib%C3%A1rruri" title="Dolores Ibárruri">Dolores Ibárruri</a> were some of the first female deputies and <a href="/wiki/Federica_Montseny" title="Federica Montseny">Federica Montseny</a> one of the first female ministers in the world. In the worsening economic situation of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression#Spain" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, Spanish politics became increasingly chaotic and violent.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_Civil_War_and_dictatorship">Spanish Civil War and dictatorship</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Revolution_of_1936" title="Spanish Revolution of 1936">Spanish Revolution of 1936</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n!_Madrid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n%21_Madrid.jpg/150px-%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n%21_Madrid.jpg" width="150" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n%21_Madrid.jpg/225px-%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n%21_Madrid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n%21_Madrid.jpg/300px-%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n%21_Madrid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2116" data-file-height="2745" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C2%A1No_pasar%C3%A1n!_Madrid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>They shall not pass!... Madrid will be the graveyard of fascism</i>. <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">Fascism</a> was on rise in Europe during Spanish Civil War.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Spanish Civil War broke out in 1936. For three years the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Nationalist faction (Spanish Civil War)">Nationalist</a> forces led by General <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> and supported by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861%E2%80%931946)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861–1946)">Fascist Italy</a> fought the <a href="/wiki/Republican_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Republican faction (Spanish Civil War)">Republican</a> side, which was supported by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, Mexico and <a href="/wiki/International_Brigades" title="International Brigades">International Brigades</a> but it was not supported by the Western powers due to the British-led policy of <a href="/wiki/Non-Intervention" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Intervention">Non-Intervention</a>. The civil war was viciously fought and there were <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War#Atrocities" title="Spanish Civil War">many atrocities committed by all sides</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">war</a> claimed the lives of over 500,000 people and caused the flight of up to a half-million citizens from the country.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[54]</a></sup> In 1939, General Franco emerged victorious and became a dictator.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg/220px-Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg/330px-Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg/440px-Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="607" data-file-height="428" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franco_eisenhower_1959_madrid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a> (Madrid 1959) in the context of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. Spain entered in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1955.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">state as established under Franco</a> was nominally <a href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" class="mw-redirect" title="Neutrality (international relations)">neutral</a> in the Second World War, although <a href="/wiki/Spain_in_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Spain in World War II">sympathetic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">the Axis</a>. The only legal party under Franco's post civil war regime was the <i><a href="/wiki/Falange" class="mw-redirect" title="Falange">Falange</a> Española Tradicionalista y de las JONS</i>, formed in 1937; the party emphasised <a href="/wiki/Falangism" title="Falangism">falangism</a>, a form of <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascism</a> that emphasised <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>. Given Franco's opposition to competing political parties, the party was renamed the National Movement (<i><a href="/wiki/Movimiento_Nacional" title="Movimiento Nacional">Movimiento Nacional</a></i>) in 1949.</p>
<p>After World War II Spain was politically and economically isolated, and was kept out of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. This changed in 1955, during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> period, when it became strategically important for the US to establish a military presence on the Iberian Peninsula as a counter to any possible move by the Soviet Union into the Mediterranean basin. In the 1960s, Spain registered an <a href="/wiki/Spanish_miracle" title="Spanish miracle">unprecedented rate of economic growth</a> which was propelled by <a href="/wiki/Spanish_miracle#Industrialisation" title="Spanish miracle">industrialisation</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_miracle#Rural_exodus" title="Spanish miracle">mass internal migration</a> from rural areas to cities and the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_miracle#Mass_tourism" title="Spanish miracle">mass tourism industry</a>. Franco's rule was also characterised by <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain#Authoritarianism" title="Francoist Spain">authoritarianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain#Nationalism" title="Francoist Spain">promotion of a unitary national identity</a>, the favouring of a very conservative form of Roman Catholicism known as <a href="/wiki/National_Catholicism" title="National Catholicism">National Catholicism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Language_policies_of_Francoist_Spain" title="Language policies of Francoist Spain">discriminatory language policies</a>.</p>
<p>In February 2016, the government of Spain announced it will rename streets named after Franco's administration officials with names of women.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_democracy">Restoration of democracy</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">Spanish transition to democracy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_society_after_the_democratic_transition" title="Spanish society after the democratic transition">Spanish society after the democratic transition</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg/200px-MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg/300px-MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg/400px-MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="802" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MITING_CNT_MONTJU%C3%8FC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Federica_Montseny" title="Federica Montseny">Federica Montseny</a> speaks at the meeting of the <a href="/wiki/Confederaci%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Trabajo" title="Confederación Nacional del Trabajo">CNT</a> in Barcelona on 1977 after 36 years of exile.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1962, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_de_Madariaga" title="Salvador de Madariaga">Salvador de Madariaga</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_International" title="Liberal International">Liberal International</a> and the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Europe" title="College of Europe">College of Europe</a>, met in the congress of the <a href="/wiki/European_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="European Movement">European Movement</a> in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> with members of the <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(politics)" title="Opposition (politics)">opposition</a> to Franco's regime inside the country and in the exile. There were 118 politicians from all factions. At the end of the meetings a resolution in favour of democracy was made.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>With Franco's death in November 1975, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">Juan Carlos</a> succeeded to the position of <a href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Spain">King of Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> in accordance with the franquist law. With the approval of the new <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">restoration of democracy</a>, the State <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolved</a> much authority to the regions and created an internal organisation based on <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous communities</a>. <a href="/wiki/Spanish_1977_Amnesty_Law" title="Spanish 1977 Amnesty Law">Spanish 1977 Amnesty Law</a> let people of Franco´s regime continue inside institutions without consequences, even responsibles of some crimes during transition to democracy like the <a href="/wiki/Massacre_of_3_March_1976_in_Vitoria" title="Massacre of 3 March 1976 in Vitoria">Massacre of 3 March 1976 in Vitoria</a> or <a href="/wiki/1977_Massacre_of_Atocha" title="1977 Massacre of Atocha">1977 Massacre of Atocha</a>.</p>
<p>In the Basque Country, moderate <a href="/wiki/Basque_nationalism" title="Basque nationalism">Basque nationalism</a> has coexisted with a <a href="/wiki/Basque_Conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque Conflict">radical nationalist movement</a> led by the armed terrorist organisation <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[59]</a></sup> The group was formed in 1959 during Franco's rule but has continued to wage its violent campaign even after the restoration of democracy and the return of a large measure of regional autonomy. On 23 February 1981, rebel elements among the security forces seized the Cortes in an attempt to impose <a href="/wiki/23-F" title="23-F">a military backed government</a>. King Juan Carlos took personal command of the military and successfully ordered the coup plotters, via national television, to surrender.</p>
<p>During the 1980s the democratic restoration made possible a growing open society. New cultural movements based on freedom appeared, like <a href="/wiki/La_Movida_Madrile%C3%B1a" title="La Movida Madrileña">La Movida Madrileña</a> and a culture of human rights arose with <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Peces-Barba" title="Gregorio Peces-Barba">Gregorio Peces-Barba</a>. On 30 May 1982 Spain joined <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, following a referendum after a strong social opposition. That year the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Socialist Workers Party">Spanish Socialist Workers Party</a> (PSOE) came to power, the first left-wing government in 43 years. In 1986 Spain joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>, which later became the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The PSOE was replaced in government by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">Partido Popular</a> (PP) in 1996 after scandals around participation of the government of <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Felipe González">Felipe González</a> in the <a href="/wiki/GAL_(paramilitary_group)" title="GAL (paramilitary group)">Dirty war against ETA</a>; at that point the PSOE had served almost 14 consecutive years in office.</p>
<p>On 1 January 2002, Spain fully adopted the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, and Spain experienced strong economic growth, well above the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> average during the early 2000s. However, well publicised concerns issued by many economic commentators at the height of the boom warned that extraordinary property prices and a high foreign trade deficit were likely to lead to a painful economic collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spain has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> since 1986</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2002 <a href="/wiki/Prestige_oil_spill" title="Prestige oil spill">Prestige oil spill</a> happened with big ecological consequences in the Spanish atlantic coastline. In 2003 <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Aznar</a> supported US president <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> in its <a href="/wiki/Preventive_war" title="Preventive war">preventive war</a> against <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Sadam Hussein´s Iraq</a>. A strong movement against war rose in Spanish society. On 11 March 2004 a local <a href="/wiki/Islamist" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamist">Islamist</a> terrorist group inspired by <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a> carried out the largest terrorist attack in Spanish history when they killed 191 people and wounded more than 1,800 others by <a href="/wiki/11_March_2004_Madrid_train_bombings" class="mw-redirect" title="11 March 2004 Madrid train bombings">bombing commuter trains</a> in Madrid.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[61]</a></sup> Though initial suspicions focused on the Basque terrorist group <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a>, evidence soon emerged indicating Islamist involvement. Because of the proximity of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_general_election,_2004" title="Spanish general election, 2004">2004 election</a>, the issue of responsibility quickly became a political controversy, with the main competing parties PP and PSOE exchanging accusations over the handling of the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[62]</a></sup> At 14 March elections, PSOE, led by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero">José Luis Rodríguez Zapatero</a> won the elections.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg/220px-Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg/330px-Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg/440px-Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Go_Spanish_revolution_-_Indignados.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Puerta_del_Sol" title="Puerta del Sol">Puerta del Sol</a> square in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, shown here on 20 May 2011, became a focal point and a symbol during the protests.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The proportion of <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Spain#Currently" title="Immigration to Spain">Spain's foreign born population</a> increased rapidly from around 1 in 50 in 2000 to almost 1 in 8 in 2010 but has since declined. In 2005 the Spanish government legalised <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Spain" title="Same-sex marriage in Spain">same sex marriage</a>. Decentralisation was supported with much resistance of Constitutional Court and conservative opposition, so did gender politics like quotas or the law against gender violence. Government talks with ETA happened, and the band announced its permanent cease of violence in 2010.</p>
<p>The bursting of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_property_bubble" title="Spanish property bubble">Spanish property bubble</a> in 2008 led to the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9316_Spanish_financial_crisis" title="2008–16 Spanish financial crisis">2008–16 Spanish financial crisis</a> and high levels of <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, cuts in government spending and <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a> in <a href="/wiki/Royal_family" title="Royal family">Royal family</a> and <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> served as a backdrop to the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Spanish_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011–12 Spanish protests">2011–12 Spanish protests</a>. <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independentism" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan independentism">Catalan independentism</a> was also on rise. In 2011 <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a>'s conservative <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> won elections with 44.6% of votes and Rajoy became the Spanish Prime Minister after having been the leader of the opposition from 2004 to 2011 with a program of cutting social spends. On 19 June 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">monarch</a>, Juan Carlos, abdicated in favour of his son, who became <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Felipe VI">Felipe VI</a>. Bipartidism in Spanish politics got to an end with the entrance of new forces in representative institutions. In 2015, <a href="/wiki/Left-wing" class="mw-redirect" title="Left-wing">left-wing</a> <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayors</a> got control of biggest cities in the country as former judge and former co-founder of the labour law office where the <a href="/wiki/1977_Massacre_of_Atocha" title="1977 Massacre of Atocha">1977 Massacre of Atocha</a> took place <a href="/wiki/Manuela_Carmena" title="Manuela Carmena">Manuela Carmena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, co-founder and spokesperson of the <a href="/wiki/Plataforma_de_Afectados_por_la_Hipoteca" title="Plataforma de Afectados por la Hipoteca">Platform for People Affected by Mortgages</a> <a href="/wiki/Ada_Colau" title="Ada Colau">Ada Colau</a> in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">Zaragoza</a>, the first time that happens since the Spanish Second Republic. Even though, in general election of the same year, conservative People's Party revalidated its majority in the parliament.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Spain" title="Geography of Spain">Geography of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spain_topo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Spain_topo.jpg/220px-Spain_topo.jpg" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Spain_topo.jpg/330px-Spain_topo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Spain_topo.jpg/440px-Spain_topo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="1197" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spain_topo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Topographic map of Spain</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At 505,992&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (195,365&#160;sq&#160;mi), Spain is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_outlying_territories_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and outlying territories by area">fifty-second largest country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Area_and_population_of_European_countries" title="Area and population of European countries">Europe's fourth largest country</a>. It is some 47,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (18,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) smaller than France and 81,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (31,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) larger than the US state of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. Mount <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>) is the highest mountain peak in Spain and is the third largest volcano in the world from its base. Spain is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental country</a>.</p>
<p>Spain lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/26th_parallel_north" title="26th parallel north">26°</a> and <a href="/wiki/44th_parallel_north" title="44th parallel north">44° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_meridian_west" title="19th meridian west">19° W</a> and <a href="/wiki/5th_meridian_east" title="5th meridian east">5° E</a>.</p>
<p>On the west, Spain is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>; on the south, it is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> (a <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territory">British overseas territory</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, through its <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclaves</a> in North Africa (<a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>, and the peninsula of <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%B3n_de_V%C3%A9lez_de_la_Gomera" title="Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera">Vélez de la Gomera</a>). On the northeast, along the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> mountain range, it is bordered by France and the <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">Principality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>. Along the Pyrenees in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Girona" title="Province of Girona">Girona</a>, a small exclave town called <a href="/wiki/Ll%C3%ADvia" title="Llívia">Llívia</a> is surrounded by France.</p>
<p>Extending to 1,214&#160;km (754&#160;mi), the <a href="/wiki/Portugal%E2%80%93Spain_border" title="Portugal–Spain border">Portugal–Spain border</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_by_land_borders" title="List of countries and territories by land borders">longest uninterrupted border</a> within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islands">Islands</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Spain" title="List of islands of Spain">List of islands of Spain</a></div>
<p>Spain also includes the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and a number of uninhabited islands on the Mediterranean side of the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, known as <span lang="es"><i><a href="/wiki/Plazas_de_soberan%C3%ADa" title="Plazas de soberanía">plazas de soberanía</a></i></span> ("places of sovereignty", or territories under [Spanish] sovereignty), such as the <a href="/wiki/Chafarinas_Islands" title="Chafarinas Islands">Chafarinas Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%B3n_de_Alhucemas" class="mw-redirect" title="Peñón de Alhucemas">Alhucemas</a>. The peninsula of <a href="/wiki/Pe%C3%B1%C3%B3n_de_V%C3%A9lez_de_la_Gomera" title="Peñón de Vélez de la Gomera">Vélez de la Gomera</a> is also regarded as a <i>plaza de soberanía</i>. The isle of <a href="/wiki/Alboran_Island" title="Alboran Island">Alborán</a>, located in the Mediterranean between Spain and North Africa, is also administered by Spain, specifically by the municipality of <a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almería">Almería</a>, Andalusia. The little <a href="/wiki/Pheasant_Island" title="Pheasant Island">Pheasant Island</a> in the River <a href="/wiki/Bidasoa" title="Bidasoa">Bidasoa</a> is a Spanish-French <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">condominium</a>.</p>
<p>Largest inhabited islands of Spain:</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teide_2_Blick_auf.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Teide_2_Blick_auf.jpg/220px-Teide_2_Blick_auf.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Teide_2_Blick_auf.jpg/330px-Teide_2_Blick_auf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Teide_2_Blick_auf.jpg/440px-Teide_2_Blick_auf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mountains_and_rivers">Mountains and rivers</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Circo_de_Soaso.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Circo_de_Soaso.jpg/220px-Circo_de_Soaso.jpg" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Circo_de_Soaso.jpg/330px-Circo_de_Soaso.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Circo_de_Soaso.jpg/440px-Circo_de_Soaso.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2822" data-file-height="1624" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Circo_de_Soaso.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ordesa_y_Monte_Perdido_National_Park" title="Ordesa y Monte Perdido National Park">Ordesa y Monte Perdido National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mainland Spain is a <a href="/wiki/Mountainous" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountainous">mountainous</a> country, dominated by high <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">plateaus</a> and mountain chains. After the Pyrenees, the main mountain ranges are the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">Cordillera Cantábrica</a> (Cantabrian Range), <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Ib%C3%A9rico" title="Sistema Ibérico">Sistema Ibérico</a> (Iberian System), <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Central" title="Sistema Central">Sistema Central</a> (Central System), <a href="/wiki/Montes_de_Toledo" title="Montes de Toledo">Montes de Toledo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Morena" title="Sierra Morena">Sierra Morena</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sistema_B%C3%A9tico" class="mw-redirect" title="Sistema Bético">Sistema Bético</a> (Baetic System) whose highest peak, the 3,478 metres (11,411&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Mulhac%C3%A9n" title="Mulhacén">Mulhacén</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(Spain)" title="Sierra Nevada (Spain)">Sierra Nevada</a>, is the highest elevation in the Iberian Peninsula. The highest point in Spain is the <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a>, a 3,718-metre (12,198&#160;ft) active <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> in the Canary Islands. The <a href="/wiki/Meseta_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="Meseta Central">Meseta Central</a> (often translated as "Inner Plateau") is a vast plateau in the heart of peninsular Spain.</p>
<p>There are several major <a href="/wiki/Rivers_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Rivers in Spain">rivers in Spain</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">Tagus</a> (<i>Tajo</i>), <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadiana_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Guadiana River">Guadiana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> (<i>Duero</i>), <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAcar_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Júcar River">Júcar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Segura" title="Segura">Segura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turia_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Turia River">Turia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minho_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Minho River">Minho</a> (<i>Miño</i>). <a href="/wiki/Alluvial_plain" title="Alluvial plain">Alluvial plains</a> are found along the coast, the largest of which is that of the Guadalquivir in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Spain" title="Climate of Spain">Climate of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Official_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_of_Spain_maded_by_AEMET.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Official_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_of_Spain_maded_by_AEMET.png/220px-Official_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_of_Spain_maded_by_AEMET.png" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fd/Official_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_of_Spain_maded_by_AEMET.png/330px-Official_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_of_Spain_maded_by_AEMET.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/fd/Official_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_of_Spain_maded_by_AEMET.png 2x" data-file-width="337" data-file-height="296" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Official_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification_of_Spain_maded_by_AEMET.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Official climatic map of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> maded by <a href="/wiki/AEMET" class="mw-redirect" title="AEMET">AEMET</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three main climatic zones can be separated, according to geographical situation and <a href="/wiki/Orography" title="Orography">orographic</a> conditions:<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[65]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a>, characterised by warm/hot and dry summers, is dominant in the peninsula. It has two varieties: <i>Csa</i> and <i>Csb</i> according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>.
<ul>
<li>The <i>Csa</i> zone is associated to areas with hot summers. It is predominant in the Mediterranean and Southern Atlantic coast and inland throughout <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> and much, if not most, of the centre of the country. The <i>Csa</i> zone covers climatic zones with both relatively warm and cold winters which are considered extremely different to each other at a local level, reason for which Köppen classification is often eschewed within Spain. Local climatic maps generally divide the Mediterranean zone (which covers most of the country) between warm-winter and cold-winter zones, rather than according to summer temperatures.</li>
<li>The <i>Csb</i> zone has warm rather than hot summers, and extends to additional cool-winter areas not typically associated with a Mediterranean climate, such as much of central and northern-central of Spain (e.g. western <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile–León</a>, northeastern <a href="/wiki/Castilla-La_Mancha" title="Castilla-La Mancha">Castilla-La Mancha</a> and northern <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Madrid" title="Community of Madrid">Madrid</a>) and into much rainier areas (notably <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>). Note areas with relatively high rainfall such as Galicia are not considered Mediterranean under local classifications, but classed as oceanic.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (<i>BSk</i>, <i>BSh</i>), is predominant in the southeastern quarter of the country, but is also widespread in other areas of Spain. It covers most of the <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Murcia" title="Region of Murcia">Region of Murcia</a>, southern <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a> and eastern Andalusia, where true hot desert climates also exist. Further to the north, it is predominant in the upper and mid reaches of the <a href="/wiki/Ebro" title="Ebro">Ebro</a> valley, which crosses southern <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a>, central Aragon and western Catalonia. It also is found in Madrid, Extremadura, Castilla-La Mancha, and some locations of western Andalusia. The dry season extends beyond the summer and average temperature depends on altitude and latitude.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<i>Cfb</i>), located in the northern quarter of the country, especially in the Atlantic region (<a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">Cantabria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a>, and partly Galicia and Castile–León). Additionally it is also found in northern Navarre, in most highlands areas along the <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Ib%C3%A9rico" title="Sistema Ibérico">Iberian System</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenean</a> valleys, where a humid subtropical variant (<i>Cfa</i>) also occurs. Winter and summer temperatures are influenced by the ocean, and have no seasonal drought.</li>
</ul>
<p>Apart from these main types, other sub-types can be found, like the <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climates</a> (<i>Dfc</i>, <i>Dfb</i> / <i>Dsc</i>, <i>Dsb</i>) in the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> as well as parts of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Cant%C3%A1brica" class="mw-redirect" title="Cordillera Cantábrica">Cantabrian Range</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Central" title="Sistema Central">Central System</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Nevada_(Spain)" title="Sierra Nevada (Spain)">Sierra Nevada</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sistema_Ib%C3%A9rico" title="Sistema Ibérico">Iberian System</a>, and a typical <a href="/wiki/Desert_climate" title="Desert climate">desert climate</a> (<i>BWk</i>, <i>BWh</i>) in the zone of Almería, Murcia and eastern <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>. Low-lying areas of the Canary Islands average above 18.0&#160;°C (64.4&#160;°F) during their coldest month, thus having a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna_and_flora">Fauna and flora</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg/220px-Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg/330px-Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg/440px-Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1996" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberian_Wolf_AdF_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Iberian_Wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberian Wolf">Iberian Wolf</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">fauna</a> presents a wide diversity that is due in large part to the geographical position of the Iberian peninsula between the Atlantic and the Mediterranean and between <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, and the great diversity of habitats and <a href="/wiki/Biotopes" class="mw-redirect" title="Biotopes">biotopes</a>, the result of a considerable variety of climates and well differentiated regions.</p>
<p>The vegetation of Spain is varied due to several factors including the diversity of the relief, the climate and <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a>. Spain includes different <a href="/wiki/Phytogeographic" class="mw-redirect" title="Phytogeographic">phytogeographic</a> regions, each with its own floristic characteristics resulting largely from the interaction of climate, topography, soil type and fire, <a href="/wiki/Biotic_component" title="Biotic component">biotic</a> factors.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Spain" title="Politics of Spain">Politics of Spain</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg/220px-Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg/330px-Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg/440px-Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="2916" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Real_Jardines.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Palace_of_Madrid" title="Royal Palace of Madrid">Royal Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a> of the EIU, Spain is one of the 20 full democracies in the world.</p>
<p>The Spanish Constitution of 1978 is the culmination of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">Spanish transition to democracy</a>. The constitutional history of Spain dates back to the constitution of 1812. Impatient with the slow pace of democratic political reforms in 1976 and 1977, Spain's new King Juan Carlos, known for his formidable personality, dismissed <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Arias_Navarro" title="Carlos Arias Navarro">Carlos Arias Navarro</a> and appointed the reformer <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez" title="Adolfo Suárez">Adolfo Suárez</a> as Prime Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-From_Dictatorship_to_Democracy_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-From_Dictatorship_to_Democracy-78">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spain.27s_fast-living_king_turns_70_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spain.27s_fast-living_king_turns_70-79">[67]</a></sup> The resulting <a href="/wiki/Spanish_general_election,_1977" title="Spanish general election, 1977">general election in 1977</a> convened the <i><a href="/wiki/Constituent_Cortes" title="Constituent Cortes">Constituent Cortes</a></i> (the Spanish Parliament, in its capacity as a constitutional assembly) for the purpose of drafting and approving the constitution of 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[68]</a></sup> After a national referendum on 6 December 1978, 88% of voters approved of the new constitution.</p>
<p>As a result, Spain is now composed of 17 <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous communities</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain#Autonomous_cities_and_.22plazas_de_soberan.C3.ADa.22" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous cities</a> with varying degrees of autonomy thanks to its Constitution, which nevertheless explicitly states the indivisible unity of the Spanish nation. The constitution also specifies that Spain has no state religion and that all are free to practice and believe as they wish.</p>
<p>The Spanish administration approved legislation in 2007 aimed at furthering <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">equality between genders</a> in Spanish political and economic life (Gender Equality Act).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[70]</a></sup> However, in the legislative branch, as of July 2010 only 128 of the 350 members of the Congress were women (36.3%).<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[71]</a></sup> It places Spain 13th on a list of countries ranked by proportion of women in the <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a>. In the Senate, the ratio is even lower, since there are only 79 women out of 263 (30.0%).<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[72]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Gender_Empowerment_Measure" title="Gender Empowerment Measure">Gender Empowerment Measure</a> of Spain in the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a> is 0.794, 12th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Spain" title="Government of Spain">Government of Spain</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spanish_monarchs" title="List of Spanish monarchs">List of Spanish monarchs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monarchs_of_Spain_family_tree" title="Monarchs of Spain family tree">Monarchs of Spain family tree</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Congreso_de_los_Diputados_(Espa%C3%B1a)_14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg/220px-Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg/330px-Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg/440px-Congreso_de_los_Diputados_%28Espa%C3%B1a%29_14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Congreso_de_los_Diputados_(Espa%C3%B1a)_14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Deputies_(Spain)" title="Congress of Deputies (Spain)">Congress of Deputies</a>, Madrid.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spain is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, with a hereditary <a href="/wiki/Monarch" title="Monarch">monarch</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral parliament">bicameral parliament</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">Cortes Generales</a></i> (General Courts). The executive branch consists of a <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of Spain">Council of Ministers of Spain</a> presided over by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain#Royal_Nomination.2C_Congressional_Confirmation" title="Prime Minister of Spain">nominated and appointed</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">monarch</a> and confirmed by the Congress of Deputies following legislative elections. By political custom established by King Juan Carlos since the ratification of the 1978 Constitution, the king's nominees have all been from parties who maintain a plurality of seats in the Congress.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Legislative_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative branch">legislative branch</a> is made up of the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Deputies_(Spain)" title="Congress of Deputies (Spain)">Congress of Deputies</a> (<i>Congreso de los Diputados</i>) with 350 members, elected by popular vote on block lists by proportional representation to serve four-year terms, and a <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Senate" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Senate">Senate</a> (<i>Senado</i>) with 259 seats of which 208 are directly elected by popular vote and the other 51 appointed by the regional legislatures to also serve four-year terms.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Head of State</b>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">King</a> <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Felipe VI</a>, since 19 June 2014</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>Head of Government</b>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Spain" title="Prime Minister of Spain">Prime Minister of Spain</a> (<i>Presidente del Gobierno</i>, literally <i>President of the Government</i>): <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy Brey</a>, elected 20 November 2011.
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/First_Vice_President_of_the_Government_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Vice President of the Government (Spain)">Deputy Prime Minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ministry_for_the_Presidency_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry for the Presidency (Spain)">Minister for the Presidency</a>: <a href="/wiki/Soraya_S%C3%A1enz_de_Santamar%C3%ADa" title="Soraya Sáenz de Santamaría">Soraya Sáenz de Santamaría</a>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><b>Cabinet</b>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of Spain">Council of Ministers</a> (<i>Consejo de Ministros</i>) designated by the Prime Minister.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Spain is organisationally structured as a so-called <i>Estado de las Autonomías</i> ("State of Autonomies"); it is one of the most <a href="/wiki/Decentralised" class="mw-redirect" title="Decentralised">decentralised</a> countries in Europe, along with Switzerland, Germany and Belgium;<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[74]</a></sup> for example, all autonomous communities have their own elected parliaments, governments, public administrations, budgets, and resources. Health and education systems among others are managed regionally, and in addition, the Basque Country and Navarre also manage their own public finances based on <a href="/wiki/Fuero" title="Fuero">foral</a> provisions. In Catalonia, the Basque Country, Navarre and the Canary Islands, a full-fledged autonomous police corps replaces some of the State police functions (see <a href="/wiki/Mossos_d%27Esquadra" title="Mossos d'Esquadra">Mossos d'Esquadra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ertzaintza" title="Ertzaintza">Ertzaintza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Foral" title="Policía Foral">Policía Foral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Canaria" title="Policía Canaria">Policía Canaria</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Spain" title="Human rights in Spain">Human rights in Spain</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Spain" title="LGBT rights in Spain">LGBT rights in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG/220px-Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG/330px-Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG/440px-Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Europride_2007_Madrid.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Europride" title="Europride">Europride</a> festival 2007 in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Government respects the <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> of its citizens; although there are a few problems in some areas, the law and judiciary provide effective means of addressing individual instances of abuse. There are allegations that a few members of the security forces abused detainees and mistreated foreigners and illegal immigrants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> (AI), government investigations of such alleged abuses are often lengthy and punishments were light.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Violence against women was a problem, which the Government took steps to address.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Spain provides one of the highest degrees of liberty in the world for its <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> community. Among the countries studied by <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> in 2013, Spain is rated first in acceptance of homosexuality, with an 88% of society supporting the gay community compared to 11% who do not.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Political_divisions_of_Spain" title="Political divisions of Spain">Political divisions of Spain</a></div>
<p>The Spanish State is integrated by 17 autonomous communities and 2 autonomous cities, both groups being the highest or first-order administrative division in the country. Autonomous communities are integrated by provinces, of which there are 50 in total, and in turn, provinces are integrated by municipalities. In Catalonia, two additional divisions exist, the <i>comarques</i> (sing. <i>comarca</i>) and the <i>vegueries</i> (sing. <i>vegueria</i>) both of which have administrative powers; <i>comarques</i> being aggregations of municipalities, and the <i>vegueries</i> being aggregations of <i>comarques</i>. The concept of a <i>comarca</i> exists in all autonomous communities, however, unlike Catalonia, these are merely historical or geographical subdivisions.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomous_communities">Autonomous communities</span></h4>
