</div>
<p>Spain's autonomous communities are the first level administrative divisions of the country. They were created after the current constitution came into effect (in 1978) in recognition of the right to self-government of the "<a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain"><i>nationalities</i> and regions of Spain</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[76]</a></sup> The autonomous communities were to be integrated into adjacent provinces with common historical, cultural, and economical traits. This territorial organisation, based on <a href="/wiki/Devolution" title="Devolution">devolution</a>, is literally known in Spain as the "State of Autonomies".</p>
<p>The basic institutional law of each autonomous community is the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">Statute of Autonomy</a>. The Statutes of Autonomy establish the name of the community according to its historical and contemporary identity, the limits of its territories, the name and organisation of the institutions of government and the rights they enjoy according to the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>The governments of all autonomous communities must be based on a division of powers comprising:</p>
<ul>
<li>a legislative assembly whose members must be elected by <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> according to the system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> and in which all areas that integrate the territory are fairly represented;</li>
<li>a government council, with executive and administrative functions headed by a president, elected by the Legislative Assembly and nominated by the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Spain">King of Spain</a>;</li>
<li>a supreme court, under the supreme court of Spain, which heads the judiciary in the autonomous community.</li>
</ul>
<p>Catalonia, Galicia and the Basque Country, which identified themselves as <i>nationalities</i> were granted self-government through a rapid process. Andalusia also took that denomination in its first Statute of Autonomy, even though it followed the longer process stipulated in the constitution for the rest of the country. Progressively, other communities in revisions to their Statutes of Autonomy have also taken that denomination in accordance to their historical and modern identities, such as the Valencian Community,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[78]</a></sup> the Canary Islands,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[79]</a></sup> the Balearic Islands,<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[80]</a></sup> and Aragon.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The autonomous communities have wide legislative and executive autonomy, with their own <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliaments</a> and regional governments. The distribution of powers may be different for every community, as laid out in their Statutes of Autonomy, since devolution was intended to be asymmetrical. Only two communities—the Basque Country and Navarre—have full fiscal autonomy. Aside of fiscal autonomy, the <i>nationalities</i>—Andalusia, the Basque Country, Catalonia, and Galicia—were devolved more powers than the rest of the communities, among them the ability of the regional president to dissolve the parliament and call for elections at any time. In addition, the Basque Country, Catalonia and Navarre have police corps of their own: <a href="/wiki/Ertzaintza" title="Ertzaintza">Ertzaintza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mossos_d%27Esquadra" title="Mossos d'Esquadra">Mossos d'Esquadra</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Polic%C3%ADa_Foral" title="Policía Foral">Policía Foral</a> respectively. Other communities have more limited forces or none at all, like the <i>Policía Autónoma Andaluza</i><sup id="cite_ref-cartujo_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cartujo-94">[82]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> or the <a href="/wiki/BESCAM" title="BESCAM">BESCAM</a> in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Salo_de_Cent.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Salo_de_Cent.jpg/220px-Salo_de_Cent.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Salo_de_Cent.jpg/330px-Salo_de_Cent.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Salo_de_Cent.jpg/440px-Salo_de_Cent.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="900" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Salo_de_Cent.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hall of the <a href="/wiki/Consell_de_Cent" title="Consell de Cent">Consell de Cent</a>, local body of <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> between the 13th and 18th centuries.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nonetheless, recent amendments to existing Statutes of Autonomy or the promulgation of new Statutes altogether, have reduced the asymmetry between the powers originally granted to the <i>nationalities</i> and the rest of the regions.</p>
<p>Finally, along with the 17 autonomous communities, two autonomous cities are also part of the State of Autonomies and are first-order territorial divisions: <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>. These are two exclaves located in the northern African coast.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Provinces_and_municipalities">Provinces and municipalities</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">Provinces of Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">Municipalities of Spain</a></div>
<p>Autonomous communities are subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">provinces</a>, which served as their territorial building blocks. In turn, provinces are integrated by <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">municipalities</a>. The existence of both the provinces and the municipalities is guaranteed and protected by the constitution, not necessarily by the Statutes of Autonomy themselves. Municipalities are granted autonomy to manage their internal affairs, and provinces are the territorial divisions designed to carry out the activities of the State.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>The current provincial division structure is based—with minor changes—on the <a href="/wiki/1833_territorial_division_of_Spain" title="1833 territorial division of Spain">1833 territorial division</a> by <a href="/wiki/Javier_de_Burgos" title="Javier de Burgos">Javier de Burgos</a>, and in all, the Spanish territory is divided into 50 provinces. The communities of Asturias, Cantabria, La Rioja, the Balearic Islands, Madrid, Murcia and Navarre are the only communities that are integrated by a single province, which is coextensive with the community itself. In these cases, the administrative institutions of the province are replaced by the governmental institutions of the community.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Spain" title="Foreign relations of Spain">Foreign relations of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cumbre_del_G20_en_Los_Cabos,_M%C3%A9xico.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Cumbre_del_G20_en_Los_Cabos%2C_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/220px-Cumbre_del_G20_en_Los_Cabos%2C_M%C3%A9xico.jpg" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Cumbre_del_G20_en_Los_Cabos%2C_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/330px-Cumbre_del_G20_en_Los_Cabos%2C_M%C3%A9xico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Cumbre_del_G20_en_Los_Cabos%2C_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/440px-Cumbre_del_G20_en_Los_Cabos%2C_M%C3%A9xico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1890" data-file-height="1190" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">Mariano Rajoy</a> in a G-20 Summit in Mexico. Spain is a permanent guest of the <a href="/wiki/G-20" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20">G-20</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg/220px-Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg/330px-Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg/440px-Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2300" data-file-height="1215" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cumbre_Iberoamericana_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Summit" title="Ibero-American Summit">Ibero-American Summit</a>, in <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">San Salvador</a>, 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the return of democracy following the death of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Franco</a> in 1975, Spain's <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> priorities were to break out of the diplomatic isolation of the <a href="/wiki/Spain_under_Franco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spain under Franco">Franco years</a> and expand <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplomatic relations">diplomatic relations</a>, enter the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Community</a>, and define security relations with the West.</p>
<p>As a member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> since 1982, Spain has established itself as a participant in multilateral international security activities. Spain's EU membership represents an important part of its foreign policy. Even on many international issues beyond western Europe, Spain prefers to co-ordinate its efforts with its EU partners through the European political co-operation mechanisms.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (March 2015)">vague</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Spain has maintained its special relations with <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>. Its policy emphasises the concept of an <a href="/wiki/Ibero-America" title="Ibero-America">Ibero-American</a> community, essentially the renewal of the historically liberal concept of <i>"<a href="/wiki/Hispanidad" title="Hispanidad">Hispanidad</a>"</i> or <i>"<a href="/wiki/Hispanism" title="Hispanism">Hispanismo</a>"</i>, as it is often referred to in English, which has sought to link the Iberian Peninsula with Hispanic America through language, commerce, history and culture.</p>
<dl>
<dt>Territorial disputes</dt>
</dl>
<p><a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">Spain claims Gibraltar</a>, a 6-square-kilometre (2.3&#160;sq&#160;mi) <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territories">Overseas Territory of the United Kingdom</a> in the southernmost part of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>. Then a Spanish town, it was conquered by an Anglo-Dutch force in 1704 during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> on behalf of <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Archduke Charles</a>, pretender to the Spanish throne.</p>
<p>The legal situation concerning Gibraltar was settled in 1713 by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>, in which Spain ceded the territory in perpetuity to the British Crown<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[84]</a></sup> stating that, should the British abandon this post, it would be offered to Spain first. Since the 1940s Spain has called for the return of Gibraltar. The overwhelming majority of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarians" title="Gibraltarians">Gibraltarians</a> strongly oppose this, along with any proposal of shared sovereignty.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[85]</a></sup> UN resolutions call on the United Kingdom and Spain, both EU members, to reach an agreement over the status of Gibraltar.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Spanish claim makes a distinction between the <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_the_isthmus_between_Gibraltar_and_Spain" title="Disputed status of the isthmus between Gibraltar and Spain">isthmus</a> that connects the Rock to the Spanish mainland on the one hand, and the Rock and city of Gibraltar on the other. While the Rock and city were ceded by the Treaty of Utrecht, Spain asserts that the "occupation of the isthmus is illegal and against the principles of <a href="/wiki/International_Law" class="mw-redirect" title="International Law">International Law</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[88]</a></sup> The United Kingdom relies on <i>de facto</i> arguments of possession by <a href="/wiki/Prescription_(sovereignty_transfer)" title="Prescription (sovereignty transfer)">prescription</a> in relation to the isthmus,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[89]</a></sup> as there has been "continuous possession [of the isthmus] over a long period".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[90]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg/220px-Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg" width="220" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg/330px-Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg/440px-Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2532" data-file-height="2342" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Combattantes_sahraouies_du_Front_Polisario.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic</a> army. According to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, Spain is the administrative power of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> de iure.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[91]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another claim by Spain is about the <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>, a claim not recognised by Portugal. Spain claims that they are rocks rather than islands, therefore claiming that there is no Portuguese territorial waters around the disputed islands. On 5 July 2013, Spain sent a letter to the UN expressing these views.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Spain claims the sovereignty over the <a href="/wiki/Perejil_Island" title="Perejil Island">Perejil Island</a>, a small, uninhabited rocky <a href="/wiki/Islet" title="Islet">islet</a> located in the South shore of the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>. The island lies 250 metres (820&#160;ft) just off the coast of Morocco, 8 kilometres (5.0&#160;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and 13.5 kilometres (8.4&#160;mi) from mainland Spain. Its sovereignty is disputed between Spain and Morocco. It was the subject of an armed incident between the two countries in 2002. The incident ended when both countries agreed to return to the <a href="/wiki/Status_quo" title="Status quo">status quo</a> ante which existed prior to the Moroccan occupation of the island. The islet is now deserted and without any sign of sovereignty.</p>
<p>Besides the Perejil Island, the Spanish-held territories claimed by other countries are two: Morocco claims the Spanish cities of Ceuta and Melilla and the <i><a href="/wiki/Plazas_de_soberan%C3%ADa" title="Plazas de soberanía">plazas de soberanía</a></i> islets off the northern coast of Africa; and Portugal does not recognise Spain's sovereignty over the territory of <a href="/wiki/Olivenza" title="Olivenza">Olivenza</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armed_Forces" title="Spanish Armed Forces">Spanish Armed Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_military_images_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Spanish_military_images_%281%29.jpg/220px-Spanish_military_images_%281%29.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Spanish_military_images_%281%29.jpg/330px-Spanish_military_images_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Spanish_military_images_%281%29.jpg/440px-Spanish_military_images_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="1110" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_military_images_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aircraft carrier/assault ship <a href="/wiki/Spanish_ship_Juan_Carlos_I_(L61)" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish ship Juan Carlos I (L61)">Juan Carlos I (L61)</a>, multirole fighter <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Eurofighter Typhoon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_CH-47_Chinook" title="Boeing CH-47 Chinook">Boeing CH-47 Chinook</a>, universal tank <a href="/wiki/Leopard_2" title="Leopard 2">Leopard 2</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The armed forces of Spain are known as the Spanish Armed Forces (<i>Fuerzas Armadas Españolas</i>). Their <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">Commander-in-chief</a> is the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Spain">King of Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Felipe VI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Armed_Forces" title="Spanish Armed Forces">Spanish Armed Forces</a> are divided into three branches:<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[95]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Army" title="Spanish Army">Army (<i>Ejército de Tierra</i>)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Navy (<i>Armada</i>)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Air_Force" title="Spanish Air Force">Air Force (<i>Ejército del Aire</i>)</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Spain" title="Economy of Spain">Economy of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Agbar_I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Torre_Agbar_I.jpg/170px-Torre_Agbar_I.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Torre_Agbar_I.jpg/255px-Torre_Agbar_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Torre_Agbar_I.jpg/340px-Torre_Agbar_I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Agbar_I.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Torre_Agbar" title="Torre Agbar">Torre Agbar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spain's <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economy</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">16th largest</a> worldwide and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_in_Europe_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of sovereign states in Europe by GDP (nominal)">5th largest</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>'s 4th largest.</p>
<p>The centre-right government of former prime minister <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="José María Aznar">José María Aznar</a> worked successfully to gain admission to the group of countries launching the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> in 1999. <a href="/wiki/Unemployment_in_Spain" title="Unemployment in Spain">Unemployment</a> stood at 7.6% in October 2006, a rate that compared favourably to many other European countries, and especially with the early 1990s when it stood at over 20%. Perennial weak points of Spain's economy include high inflation,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[96]</a></sup> a large <a href="/wiki/Underground_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Underground economy">underground economy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[97]</a></sup> and an education system which OECD reports place among the poorest for developed countries, together with the United States and UK.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the mid-1990s the economy had recommenced the growth that had been disrupted by the global recession of the early 1990s. The strong economic growth helped the government to reduce the government debt as a percentage of GDP and Spain's high unemployment began to drop steadily. With the government budget in balance and inflation under control Spain was admitted into the Eurozone in 1999.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/220px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/330px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/440px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="645" data-file-height="690" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Spain is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the 1990s some Spanish companies have gained multinational status, often expanding their activities in culturally close Latin America. Spain is the second biggest foreign investor there, after the United States. Spanish companies have also expanded into Asia, especially China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist2009bet_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2009bet-111">[99]</a></sup> This early global expansion is a competitive advantage over its competitors and European neighbours. The reason for this early expansion is the booming interest towards Spanish language and culture in Asia and Africa and a corporate culture that learned to take risks in unstable markets.</p>
<p>Spanish companies invested in fields like <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable energy commercialisation">renewable energy commercialisation</a> (<a href="/wiki/Iberdrola" title="Iberdrola">Iberdrola</a> was the world's largest renewable energy operator<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[100]</a></sup>), technology companies like <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica" title="Telefónica">Telefónica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abengoa" title="Abengoa">Abengoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mondragon_Corporation" title="Mondragon Corporation">Mondragon Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Movistar" title="Movistar">Movistar</a>, Hisdesat, <a href="/wiki/Indra_Sistemas" title="Indra Sistemas">Indra</a>, train manufacturers like <a href="/wiki/Construcciones_y_Auxiliar_de_Ferrocarriles" title="Construcciones y Auxiliar de Ferrocarriles">CAF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Talgo" title="Talgo">Talgo</a>, global corporations such as the textile company <a href="/wiki/Inditex" title="Inditex">Inditex</a>, petroleum companies like <a href="/wiki/Repsol" title="Repsol">Repsol</a> and infrastructure, with six of the ten biggest international construction firms specialising in transport being Spanish, like <a href="/wiki/Ferrovial" title="Ferrovial">Ferrovial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acciona" title="Acciona">Acciona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grupo_ACS" class="mw-redirect" title="Grupo ACS">ACS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obrasc%C3%B3n_Huarte_Lain" title="Obrascón Huarte Lain">OHL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fomento_de_Construcciones_y_Contratas" title="Fomento de Construcciones y Contratas">FCC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist2009big_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist2009big-113">[101]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg/220px-Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg" width="220" height="75" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg/330px-Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg/440px-Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5114" data-file-height="1750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Guggenheim_Bilbao_06_2012_Panorama_2680.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The urban transformation of <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> has been hailed as an example of "<a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart city</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[104]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005 the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a> survey placed Spain among the top 10 in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[105]</a></sup> In 2013 the same survey (now called the "Where-to-be-born index"), ranked Spain 28th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Bilbao" title="Bilbao">Bilbao</a> was awarded with the <a href="/wiki/Lee_Kuan_Yew_World_City_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Lee Kuan Yew World City Prize">Lee Kuan Yew World City Prize</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[107]</a></sup> and its mayor at the time, <a href="/wiki/I%C3%B1aki_Azkuna" title="Iñaki Azkuna">Iñaki Azkuna</a>, was awarded the <a href="/wiki/World_Mayor" title="World Mayor">World Mayor</a> Prize in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[108]</a></sup> The Basque capital city of <a href="/wiki/Vitoria-Gasteiz" title="Vitoria-Gasteiz">Vitoria-Gasteiz</a> received the <a href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital_Award" title="European Green Capital Award">European Green Capital Award</a> in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Spain" title="Agriculture in Spain">Agriculture in Spain</a></div>
<p>Crop areas were farmed in two highly diverse manners. Areas relying on non-irrigated cultivation (<i>secano</i>), which made up 85% of the entire crop area, depended solely on rainfall as a source of water. They included the humid regions of the north and the northwest, as well as vast arid zones that had not been irrigated. The much more productive regions devoted to irrigated cultivation (<i>regadío</i>) accounted for 3 million hectares in 1986, and the government hoped that this area would eventually double, as it already had doubled since 1950. Particularly noteworthy was the development in <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Almer%C3%ADa" title="Province of Almería">Almería</a>—one of the most arid and desolate provinces of Spain—of winter crops of various fruits and vegetables for export to Europe.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg/220px-Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg/330px-Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg/440px-Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vi%C3%B1edo-en-Ventosa-LaRioja.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyard</a> growing grapes for <a href="/wiki/Rioja_wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Rioja wine">Rioja wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Rioja,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="La Rioja, Spain">La Rioja</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Though only about 17% of Spain's cultivated land was irrigated, it was estimated to be the source of between 40–45% of the gross value of crop production and of 50% of the value of agricultural exports. More than half of the irrigated area was planted in <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fruit_tree" title="Fruit tree">fruit trees</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a>. Other agricultural products that benefited from irrigation included <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beet" title="Sugar beet">sugar beets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legume" title="Legume">legumes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Olive tree">olive trees</a>, mangos, <a href="/wiki/Strawberries" class="mw-redirect" title="Strawberries">strawberries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fodder" title="Fodder">fodder</a> grasses. Depending on the nature of the crop, it was possible to harvest two successive crops in the same year on about 10% of the country's irrigated land.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Citrus_fruit" class="mw-redirect" title="Citrus fruit">Citrus fruits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vegetable" title="Vegetable">vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cereal_grain" class="mw-redirect" title="Cereal grain">cereal grains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a>—Spain's traditional agricultural products—continued to be important in the 1980s. In 1983 they represented 12%, 12%, 8%, 6%, and 4%, respectively, of the country's agricultural production. Because of the changed diet of an increasingly affluent population, there was a notable increase in the consumption of <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a>. <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">Meat</a> production for domestic consumption became the single most important agricultural activity, accounting for 30% of all farm-related production in 1983. Increased attention to livestock was the reason that Spain became a net importer of grains. Ideal growing conditions, combined with proximity to important north European markets, made citrus fruits Spain's leading export. Fresh vegetables and fruits produced through intensive irrigation farming also became important export commodities, as did <a href="/wiki/Sunflower_seed_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunflower seed oil">sunflower seed oil</a> that was produced to compete with the more expensive olive oils in oversupply throughout the Mediterranean countries of the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Community</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Spain" title="Tourism in Spain">Tourism in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Benidorm2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Benidorm2.jpg/220px-Benidorm2.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Benidorm2.jpg/330px-Benidorm2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Benidorm2.jpg/440px-Benidorm2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="1728" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Benidorm2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Benidorm" title="Benidorm">Benidorm</a>, one of Europe's largest coastal tourist destinations</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The climate of Spain, its geographic location, popular coastlines, diverse landscapes, historical legacy, vibrant culture and excellent infrastructure, has made Spain's international tourist industry among the largest in the world. In the last five decades, international tourism in Spain has grown to become the second largest in the world in terms of spending, worth approximately 40&#160;billion Euros or about 5% of GDP in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-guru_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guru-122">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Spain" title="Energy in Spain">Energy in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg/220px-Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg/330px-Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg/440px-Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Enerx%C3%ADa_e%C3%B3lica_-_O_Pindo_-_Galicia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wind_turbine" title="Wind turbine">Wind turbines</a> in <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>. Spain is the fourth producer of <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind power</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[112]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spain is one of the world's leading countries in the development and production of renewable energy. In 2010 Spain became the <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Spain" title="Solar power in Spain">solar power</a> world leader when it overtook the United States with a massive power station plant called <a href="/wiki/Alvarado_I" title="Alvarado I">La Florida</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Badajoz" title="Badajoz">Alvarado, Badajoz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[114]</a></sup> Spain is also Europe's main producer of wind energy. In 2010 its wind turbines generated 42,976 GWh, which accounted for 16.4% of all electrical energy produced in Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Graber2005_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Graber2005-129">[117]</a></sup> On 9 November 2010, wind energy reached an instantaneous historic peak covering 53% of mainland electricity demand<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[118]</a></sup> and generating an amount of energy that is equivalent to that of 14 <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[119]</a></sup> Other renewable energies used in Spain are <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric power plant">hydroelectric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gasification_of_biomass" class="mw-redirect" title="Gasification of biomass">biomass</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marine_energy" title="Marine energy">marine</a> (2 power plants under construction).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Non-renewable energy sources used in Spain are <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">nuclear</a> (8 operative reactors), <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas power plant">gas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coal_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal power plant">coal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oil_power_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil power plant">oil</a>. Fossil fuels together generated 58% of Spain's electricity in 2009, just below the OECD mean of 61%. Nuclear power generated another 19%, and wind and hydro about 12% each.<sup id="cite_ref-SverigeE_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SverigeE-133">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Spain" title="Transport in Spain">Transport in Spain</a></div>
<p>The Spanish road system is mainly centralised, with six highways connecting <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a>, West <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a>. Additionally, there are highways along the Atlantic (<a href="/wiki/Ferrol,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferrol, Spain">Ferrol</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vigo" title="Vigo">Vigo</a>), Cantabrian (<a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> to <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebastián">San Sebastián</a>) and Mediterranean (<a href="/wiki/Girona" title="Girona">Girona</a> to <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>) coasts. Spain aims to put one&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Electric_car" title="Electric car">electric cars</a> on the road by 2014 as part of the government's plan to save energy and boost <a href="/wiki/Efficient_energy_use" title="Efficient energy use">energy efficiency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[122]</a></sup> The former Minister of Industry <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Gasc%C3%B3n" title="Miguel Sebastián Gascón">Miguel Sebastián</a> said that "the electric vehicle is the future and the engine of an industrial revolution."<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[123]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trenes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Trenes.jpg/220px-Trenes.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Trenes.jpg/330px-Trenes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Trenes.jpg/440px-Trenes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="799" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trenes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> high-speed trains.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spain has the most extensive high-speed rail network in Europe, and the second-most extensive in the world after China.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[125]</a></sup> As of October 2010, Spain has a total of 3,500&#160;km (2,174.80&#160;mi) of high-speed tracks linking <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">Málaga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a>, with the trains reaching speeds up to 300&#160;km/h (190&#160;mph). On average, the Spanish high-speed train is the fastest one in the world, followed by the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">bullet train</a> and the French <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[126]</a></sup> Regarding punctuality, it is second in the world (98.54% on-time arrival) after the Japanese Shinkansen (99%).<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[127]</a></sup> Should the aims of the ambitious <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> programme (Spanish high speed trains) be met, by 2020 Spain will have 7,000&#160;km (4,300&#160;mi) of high-speed trains linking almost all provincial cities to Madrid in less than three hours and Barcelona within four hours.</p>
<p>There are 47 public airports in Spain. The busiest one is the <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrid Airport">airport of Madrid</a> (Barajas), with 50&#160;million passengers in 2011, being the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">world's 15th busiest airport</a>, as well as the European Union's fourth busiest. The <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Barcelona Airport">airport of Barcelona</a> (El Prat) is also important, with 35&#160;million passengers in 2011, being the world's 31st-busiest airport. Other main airports are located in <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Airport" title="Palma de Mallorca Airport">Majorca</a> (23&#160;million passengers), <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_Airport" title="Málaga Airport">Málaga</a> (13&#160;million passengers), <a href="/wiki/Gran_Canaria_Airport" title="Gran Canaria Airport">Las Palmas (Gran Canaria)</a> (11&#160;million passengers), <a href="/wiki/Alicante_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Alicante Airport">Alicante</a> (10&#160;million passengers) and smaller, with the number of passengers between 4 and 10 million, for example <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_South_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenerife South Airport">Tenerife</a> (two airports), <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Airport" title="Valencia Airport">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seville_Airport" title="Seville Airport">Seville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilbao_Airport" title="Bilbao Airport">Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibiza_Airport" title="Ibiza Airport">Ibiza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lanzarote_Airport" title="Lanzarote Airport">Lanzarote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuerteventura_Airport" title="Fuerteventura Airport">Fuerteventura</a>. Also, more than 30 airports with the number of passengers below 4 million.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Spain" title="Science and technology in Spain">Science and technology in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg/220px-Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg/330px-Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg/440px-Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="737" data-file-height="491" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ing_telescopes_sunset_la_palma_july_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Roque_de_los_Muchachos_Observatory" title="Roque de los Muchachos Observatory">Roque de los Muchachos Observatory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Astrof%C3%ADsica_de_Canarias" title="Instituto de Astrofísica de Canarias">Instituto de Astrofísica de Canarias</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 19th and 20th centuries science in Spain was held back by severe political instability and consequent economic underdevelopment. Despite the conditions, some important scientists and engineers emerged. The most notable were <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Servet" class="mw-redirect" title="Miguel Servet">Miguel Servet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ram%C3%B3n_y_Cajal" title="Santiago Ramón y Cajal">Santiago Ramón y Cajal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narc%C3%ADs_Monturiol" title="Narcís Monturiol">Narcís Monturiol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celedonio_Calatayud" title="Celedonio Calatayud">Celedonio Calatayud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_la_Cierva" title="Juan de la Cierva">Juan de la Cierva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_Torres_y_Quevedo" title="Leonardo Torres y Quevedo">Leonardo Torres y Quevedo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margarita_Salas" title="Margarita Salas">Margarita Salas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Severo_Ochoa" title="Severo Ochoa">Severo Ochoa</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dd><i>See also <a href="/wiki/ASCAMM" title="ASCAMM">ASCAMM</a>, Associació Catalana d'Empreses constructores de Motlles i Matrius</i></dd>
</dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Spain" title="Water supply and sanitation in Spain">Water supply and sanitation in Spain</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">Water supply</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> in Spain is characterised by universal access and generally good service quality, while tariffs are among the lowest in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-iwahq.org_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iwahq.org-140">[128]</a></sup> Almost half of the population is served by private or mixed private-public water companies, which operate under concession contracts with municipalities. The largest of the private water companies, with a market share of about 50% of the private concessions, is Aguas de Barcelona (<a href="/wiki/Agbar" class="mw-redirect" title="Agbar">Agbar</a>). However, the large cities are all served by public companies except Barcelona and Valencia. The largest public company is <a href="/wiki/Canal_de_Isabel_II" title="Canal de Isabel II">Canal de Isabel II</a>, which serves the metropolitan area of Madrid.</p>
<p>Droughts affect water supply in Southern Spain, which increasingly is turning towards seawater <a href="/wiki/Water_desalination" class="mw-redirect" title="Water desalination">desalination</a> to meet its water needs.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Spain" title="Demographics of Spain">Demographics of Spain</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Spanish_autonomous_communities_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Spanish autonomous communities by population">List of Spanish autonomous communities by population</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hemispheric_-_Valencia,_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Hemispheric_-_Valencia%2C_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg/220px-Hemispheric_-_Valencia%2C_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Hemispheric_-_Valencia%2C_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg/330px-Hemispheric_-_Valencia%2C_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Hemispheric_-_Valencia%2C_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg/440px-Hemispheric_-_Valencia%2C_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5808" data-file-height="3227" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hemispheric_-_Valencia,_Spain_-_Jan_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>. The Mediterranean coast is the most densely inhabited area in Spain.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2008 the population of Spain officially reached 46&#160;million people, as recorded by the <i>Padrón municipal</i> (Spain's Municipal Register).<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[129]</a></sup> Spain's population density, at 91/km² (235/sq mi), is lower than that of most Western European countries and its distribution across the country is very unequal. With the exception of the region surrounding the capital, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, the most populated areas lie around the coast. The population of Spain more than doubled since 1900, when it stood at 18.6 million, principally due to the spectacular demographic boom in the 1960s and early 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Native <a href="/wiki/Spaniards" title="Spaniards">Spaniards</a> make up 88% of the total population of Spain. After the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_territories_by_fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries and territories by fertility rate">birth rate</a> plunged in the 1980s and Spain's population growth rate dropped, the population again trended upward, based initially on the return of many Spaniards who had emigrated to other European countries during the 1970s, and more recently, fuelled by large numbers of immigrants who make up 12% of the population. The immigrants originate mainly in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> (39%), <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> (16%), <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> (15%), and <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a> (4%).<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[131]</a></sup> In 2005, Spain instituted a three-month amnesty programme through which certain hitherto undocumented aliens were granted legal residency.</p>
<p>In 2008, Spain granted citizenship to 84,170 persons, mostly to people from Ecuador, Colombia and Morocco.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[132]</a></sup> A sizeable portion of foreign residents in Spain also comes from other Western and Central European countries. These are mostly British, French, German, Dutch, and Norwegian. They reside primarily on the Mediterranean coast and the Balearic islands, where many choose to live their retirement or <a href="/wiki/Telecommute" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommute">telecommute</a>.</p>
<p>Substantial populations descended from Spanish colonists and immigrants exist in other parts of the world, most notably in Latin America. Beginning in the late 15th century, large numbers of Iberian colonists settled in what became Latin America and at present most <a href="/wiki/White_Latin_American" class="mw-redirect" title="White Latin American">white Latin Americans</a> (who make up about one-third of Latin America's population) are of Spanish or Portuguese origin. Around 240,000 Spaniards emigrated in the 16th century, mostly to <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[133]</a></sup> Another 450,000 left in the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[134]</a></sup> Between 1846 and 1932 it is estimated that nearly 5&#160;million Spaniards emigrated to the Americas, especially to <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[135]</a></sup> Approximately two million Spaniards migrated to other Western European countries between 1960 and 1975. During the same period perhaps 300,000 went to Latin America.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanisation">Urbanisation</span></h3>
<table class="navbox">
<tr>
<th colspan="10" class="navbox-title">
<div style="float:right; width:6em; height:2.6em">&#160;</div>
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style="float: left;height:2.6em;">

<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Largest_cities_of_Spain" title="Template:Largest cities of Spain"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>

<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Largest_cities_of_Spain&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
