<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Peoples">Peoples</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalisms_and_regionalisms_of_Spain" title="Nationalisms and regionalisms of Spain">Nationalisms and regionalisms of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG/220px-Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG/330px-Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG/440px-Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gaiterosenoviedo.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturian</a> <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk musicians</a> with <a href="/wiki/Bagpipes" title="Bagpipes">bagpipes</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a>, in its second article, recognises contemporary <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">entities</a>—<i><a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain">nationalities</a></i> (a carefully chosen word to avoid the more politically charged "nations")—and regions, within the context of the Spanish nation. For some people, Spain's identity consists more of an overlap of different territorial and ethnolinguistic identities than of a sole Spanish identity. Indeed, some of the territorial identities may even conflict with the Spanish one. Distinct traditional identities within Spain include the <a href="/wiki/Basque_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Basque people">Basques</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan people">Catalans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician people">Galicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andalusians" title="Andalusians">Andalusians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valencian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencian people">Valencians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[142]</a></sup> although to some extent all of the 17 autonomous communities will claim a distinct local identity.</p>
<p>It is this last feature of "shared identity" between the more local level or autonomous community and the Spanish level which makes the identity question in Spain complex and far from univocal.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minority_groups">Minority groups</span></h3>
<p>Spain has a number of descendants of populations from former colonies, especially <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>. Smaller numbers of immigrants from several <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan">Sub-Saharan</a> countries have recently been settling in Spain. There are also sizeable numbers of <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> immigrants, most of whom are of <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle Eastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="South Asian">South Asian</a> and Chinese origin. The single largest group of immigrants are European; represented by large numbers of Romanians, Britons, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, French and others.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[143]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:358px;max-width:358px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Ceuta_desde_el_Monte_Hacho,_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ceuta_desde_el_Monte_Hacho%2C_2008.jpg/200px-Ceuta_desde_el_Monte_Hacho%2C_2008.jpg" width="200" height="83" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ceuta_desde_el_Monte_Hacho%2C_2008.jpg/300px-Ceuta_desde_el_Monte_Hacho%2C_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Ceuta_desde_el_Monte_Hacho%2C_2008.jpg/400px-Ceuta_desde_el_Monte_Hacho%2C_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="423" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Vista_desde_Melilla_la_Vieja.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Vista_desde_Melilla_la_Vieja.jpg/150px-Vista_desde_Melilla_la_Vieja.jpg" width="150" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Vista_desde_Melilla_la_Vieja.jpg/225px-Vista_desde_Melilla_la_Vieja.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Vista_desde_Melilla_la_Vieja.jpg/300px-Vista_desde_Melilla_la_Vieja.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2256" data-file-height="1584" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> have a big population of North African ancestry.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The arrival of the <i><a href="/wiki/Roma_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma in Spain">gitanos</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a>, began in the 16th century; estimates of the Spanish Roma population range from 750,000 to over one million.<sup id="cite_ref-Diagnostico_Social_de_la_Comunidad_Gitana_en_Espana_-_CIS_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diagnostico_Social_de_la_Comunidad_Gitana_en_Espana_-_CIS-156">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-immigration_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immigration-159">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[148]</a></sup> There are also the <i><a href="/wiki/Merchero" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchero">mercheros</a></i> (also <i>quinquis</i>), a formerly nomadic minority group. Their origin is unclear.</p>
<p>Historically, <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardi Jews</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morisco" title="Morisco">Moriscos</a> are the main minority groups originated in Spain and with a contribution to Spanish culture.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[149]</a></sup> The Spanish government is offering Spanish nationality to Sephardi Jews.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[150]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Spain" title="Immigration to Spain">Immigration to Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marbella3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Marbella3.jpg/220px-Marbella3.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Marbella3.jpg/330px-Marbella3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Marbella3.jpg/440px-Marbella3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6021" data-file-height="4014" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marbella3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Marbella" title="Marbella">Marbella</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_M%C3%A1laga" title="Province of Málaga">Málaga</a>, where Britons—who are the third biggest immigrant community in Spain—reside in large numbers.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the Spanish government there were 5.7&#160;million foreign residents in Spain in 2011, or 12% of the total population. According to residence permit data for 2011, more than 860,000 were <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanian</a>, about 770,000 were <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan people">Moroccan</a>, approximately 390,000 were British, and 360,000 were <a href="/wiki/Ecuadorian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecuadorian people">Ecuadorian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[151]</a></sup> Other sizeable foreign communities are <a href="/wiki/Colombian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Colombian people">Colombian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolivian people">Bolivian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarian</a>, and Chinese. There are more than 200,000 migrants from Sub-Saharan <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> living in Spain, principally <a href="/wiki/Senegalese_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Senegalese people">Senegaleses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Nigerian people">Nigerians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[152]</a></sup> Since 2000, Spain has experienced high <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a> as a result of immigration flows, despite a birth rate that is only half the replacement level. This sudden and ongoing inflow of immigrants, particularly those arriving illegally by sea, has caused noticeable social tension.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[153]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG/220px-Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG/330px-Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG/440px-Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bellver_Castle_2008_Palma_Mallorca_130.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca" class="mw-redirect" title="Palma de Mallorca">Palma de Mallorca</a> where a large population of <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a> live.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Within the EU, Spain had the 2nd highest immigration rate in percentage terms after <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, but by a great margin, the highest in absolute numbers, up to 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[154]</a></sup> The number of immigrants in Spain had grown up from 500,000 people in 1996 to 5.2&#160;million in 2008 out of a total population of 46&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[156]</a></sup> In 2005 alone, a regularisation programme increased the legal immigrant population by 700,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[157]</a></sup> There are a number of reasons for the high level of immigration, including Spain's cultural ties with <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, its geographical position, the porosity of its borders, the large size of its underground economy and the strength of the agricultural and construction sectors, which demand more low cost labour than can be offered by the national workforce.</p>
<p>Another statistically significant factor is the large number of residents of EU origin typically retiring to Spain's Mediterranean coast. In fact, Spain was Europe's largest absorber of migrants from 2002 to 2007, with its immigrant population more than doubling as 2.5&#160;million people arrived.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[158]</a></sup> In 2008, prior to the onset of the economic crisis, the <i>Financial Times</i> reported that Spain was the most favoured destination for Western Europeans considering a move from their own country and seeking jobs elsewhere in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, the government instituted a "Plan of Voluntary Return" which encouraged unemployed immigrants from outside the EU to return to their home countries and receive several incentives, including the right to keep their unemployment benefits and transfer whatever they contributed to the Spanish Social Security.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[160]</a></sup> The programme had little effect; during its first two months, just 1,400 immigrants took up the offer.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[161]</a></sup> What the programme failed to do, the sharp and prolonged economic crisis has done from 2010 to 2011 in that tens of thousands of immigrants have left the country due to lack of jobs. In 2011 alone, more than half a million people left Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-emigracion_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emigracion-174">[162]</a></sup> For the first time in decades the net migration rate was expected to be negative, and nine out of 10 emigrants were foreigners.<sup id="cite_ref-emigracion_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emigracion-174">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Spain" title="Languages of Spain">Languages of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_Spain.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Languages_of_Spain.svg/300px-Languages_of_Spain.svg.png" width="300" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Languages_of_Spain.svg/450px-Languages_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Languages_of_Spain.svg/600px-Languages_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="578" data-file-height="374" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Languages_of_Spain.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The languages of Spain (simplified)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spain is openly multilingual,<sup id="cite_ref-conversi_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conversi-175">[163]</a></sup> and the constitution establishes that the nation will protect "all Spaniards and the peoples of Spain in the exercise of human rights, their cultures and traditions, languages and institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-preamble_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-preamble-176">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> (<i>español</i>)—officially recognised in the constitution as <a href="/wiki/Names_given_to_the_Spanish_language" title="Names given to the Spanish language">Castilian</a> (<i>castellano</i>)—is the official language of the entire country, and it is the right and duty of every Spaniard to know the language. The constitution also establishes that "all other Spanish languages"—that is, all other languages of Spain—will also be official in their respective autonomous communities in accordance to their <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">Statutes</a>, their organic regional legislations, and that the "richness of the distinct linguistic modalities of Spain represents a patrimony which will be the object of special respect and protection."<sup id="cite_ref-third_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-third-177">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>The other official languages of Spain, co-official with Spanish are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> (<i>euskara</i>) in the <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">Basque Country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">Navarre</a>;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> (<i>català</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian Community</a>, where its distinct modality of the language is officially known as <a href="/wiki/Valencian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencian language">Valencian</a> (<i>valencià</i>); and</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a> (<i>galego</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a></li>
</ul>
<p>As a percentage of the general population, Basque is spoken by 2%, Catalan (or Valencian) by 17%, and Galician by 7% of all Spaniards.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aranese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Aranese language">Aranese</a> (<i>aranés</i>), a local variety of the <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan language</a>, has been declared co-official along with Catalan and Spanish since 2006. It is spoken only in the <i>comarca</i> of <i><a href="/wiki/Val_d%27Aran" title="Val d'Aran">Val d'Aran</a></i> by roughly 6,700 people. Other <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance</a> <a href="/wiki/Minority_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Minority languages">minority languages</a>, though not official, have special recognition, such as the Astur-Leonese group (<a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a> – <i>asturianu</i>, also called <i>bable</i> – in <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[167]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Leonese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Leonese language">Leonese</a> – <i>llionés</i> – in <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">Aragonese</a> (<i>aragonés</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North African</a> Spanish autonomous city of <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riff_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Riff language">Riff Berber</a> is spoken by a significant part of the population. In the tourist areas of the Mediterranean coast and the islands, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> are widely spoken by tourists, foreign residents, and tourism workers.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Spain" title="Education in Spain">Education in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg/150px-Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg" width="150" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg/225px-Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg/300px-Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Concepcion_Arenal_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n_Arenal" title="Concepción Arenal">Concepción Arenal</a>, defendant of the right of women to education.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>State education in Spain is free and compulsory from the age of six to sixteen. The current education system was established by the 2006 educational law, LOE (<i>Ley Orgánica de Educación</i>), or Fundamental Law for the Education.<sup id="cite_ref-LOE_juridicas_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOE_juridicas-181">[169]</a></sup> In 2014, the LOE was partially modified by the newer and controversial LOMCE law (<i>Ley Orgánica para la Mejora de la Calidad Educativa</i>), or Fundamental Law for the Improvement of the Education System, commonly called <i>Ley Wert</i> (Wert Law).<sup id="cite_ref-LOMCE_juridicas_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOMCE_juridicas-182">[170]</a></sup> Since 1970 to 2014, Spain has had seven different educational laws (LGE, LOECE, LODE, LOGSE, LOPEG, LOE and LOMCE).<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Instituci%C3%B3n_Libre_de_Ense%C3%B1anza" title="Institución Libre de Enseñanza">Institución Libre de Enseñanza</a> was an educational project that developed in Spain for the half a century of about 1876–1936 by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Giner_de_los_R%C3%ADos" title="Francisco Giner de los Ríos">Francisco Giner de los Ríos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gumersindo_de_Azc%C3%A1rate" title="Gumersindo de Azcárate">Gumersindo de Azcárate</a>. The institute was inspired by the philosophy of <a href="/wiki/Krausism" title="Krausism">Krausism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n_Arenal" title="Concepción Arenal">Concepción Arenal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ram%C3%B3n_y_Cajal" title="Santiago Ramón y Cajal">Santiago Ramón y Cajal</a> in neuroscience were in the movement.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Spain" title="Health care in Spain">Health care in Spain</a></div>
<p>The health care system of Spain (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_National_Health_System" title="Spanish National Health System">Spanish National Health System</a>) is considered one of the best in the world, in 7th position in the ranking elaborated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[172]</a></sup> The health care is public, universal and free for any legal citizen of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[173]</a></sup> The total health spending is 9.4% of the GDP, slightly above the average of 9.3% of the <a href="/wiki/OECD" class="mw-redirect" title="OECD">OECD</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Spain" title="Religion in Spain">Religion in Spain</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianity in Spain">Christianity in Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Spain" title="Islam in Spain">Islam in Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Judaism in Spain">Judaism in Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Spain" title="Hinduism in Spain">Hinduism in Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Spain" title="Bahá'í Faith in Spain">Bahá'í Faith in Spain</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
<tr style="background:#ddd">
<th colspan="5">Religions in Spain</th>
</tr>
<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
<td style="padding:0 4px;"></td>
<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>
<td style="width:100px;"></td>
<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;"></td>
<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>
</tr>

<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Catholicism</td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:SteelBlue; width:67.8%; overflow: hidden;">&#160; </div>
</td>

</tr>
<tr>

</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other Faith</td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:MediumAquaMarine; width:2.2%; overflow: hidden;">&#160; </div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.2%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">No Answer</td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
<div style="background:purple; width:2.5%; overflow: hidden;">&#160; </div>
</td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.5%</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="5" style="padding:5px">Numbers from the following source:<sup id="cite_ref-CIS_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIS-7">[4]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholicism</a> has long been the main religion of Spain, and although it no longer has official status by law, in all public schools in Spain students have to choose either a religion or ethics class. Catholicism is the religion most commonly taught, although the teaching of Islam,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[174]</a></sup> Judaism,<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[175]</a></sup> and evangelical Christianity<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[176]</a></sup> is also recognised in law. According to a June 2016 study by the Spanish Centre for Sociological Research about 68% of Spaniards self-identify as Catholics, 2% other faith, and about 27% identify with <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religion</a>. Most Spaniards do not participate regularly in religious services. This same study shows that of the Spaniards who identify themselves as religious, 59% hardly ever or never go to church, 16% go to church some times a year, 9% some time per month and 15% every Sunday or multiple times per week.<sup id="cite_ref-CIS_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIS-7">[4]</a></sup> Recent polls and surveys have revealed that <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agnosticism" title="Agnosticism">agnostics</a> comprise anywhere from 20% to 27% of the Spanish population.<sup id="cite_ref-CIS_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIS-7">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WVS_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WVS-189">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GallupInternational_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GallupInternational-190">[178]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg/170px-Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg/255px-Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg/340px-Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="3072" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Santiago.de.Compostela.Catedral.Noche.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Compostela_Cathedral" title="Santiago de Compostela Cathedral">Santiago de Compostela Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Province of A Coruña">A Coruña.</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Altogether, about 9% of the entire Spanish population attends religious services at least once per month.<sup id="cite_ref-CIS_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIS-7">[4]</a></sup> Though Spanish society has become considerably more secular in recent decades, the influx of Latin American immigrants, who tend to be strong Catholic practitioners, has helped the Catholic Church to recover.</p>
<p>There have been four Spanish <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Popes</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pope_Damasus_I" title="Pope Damasus I">Damasus I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Calixtus_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Pope Calixtus III">Calixtus III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">Alexander VI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antipope_Benedict_XIII" title="Antipope Benedict XIII">Benedict XIII</a>. Spanish mysticism was an important intellectual fight against Protestantism with <a href="/wiki/Teresa_of_%C3%81vila" title="Teresa of Ávila">Teresa of Ávila</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">reformist</a> nun, ahead. The <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> was founded by <a href="/wiki/Ignatius_of_Loyola" title="Ignatius of Loyola">Ignatius of Loyola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Javier" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Javier">Francisco Javier</a>. In the 60s of the 20th century, Jesuits <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Arrupe" title="Pedro Arrupe">Pedro Arrupe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Ellacur%C3%ADa" title="Ignacio Ellacuría">Ignacio Ellacuría</a> were inside the movement of <a href="/wiki/Liberation_Theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberation Theology">Liberation Theology</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> churches have about 1,200,000 members.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[179]</a></sup> There are about 105,000 <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> has approximately 46,000 adherents in 133 congregations in all regions of the country and has a <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Spain_Temple" title="Madrid Spain Temple">temple</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Moratalaz" title="Moratalaz">Moratalaz</a> District of Madrid.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[180]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:366px;max-width:366px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:112px;max-width:112px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Ignatius_of_Loyola_(1491-1556)_Founder_of_the_Jesuits.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/St_Ignatius_of_Loyola_%281491-1556%29_Founder_of_the_Jesuits.jpg/110px-St_Ignatius_of_Loyola_%281491-1556%29_Founder_of_the_Jesuits.jpg" width="110" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/St_Ignatius_of_Loyola_%281491-1556%29_Founder_of_the_Jesuits.jpg/165px-St_Ignatius_of_Loyola_%281491-1556%29_Founder_of_the_Jesuits.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/St_Ignatius_of_Loyola_%281491-1556%29_Founder_of_the_Jesuits.jpg/220px-St_Ignatius_of_Loyola_%281491-1556%29_Founder_of_the_Jesuits.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1956" data-file-height="3182" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:122px;max-width:122px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs.jpg/120px-Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs.jpg" width="120" height="174" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs.jpg/180px-Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs.jpg/240px-Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1159" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:FranciscusXavier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/FranciscusXavier.jpg/124px-FranciscusXavier.jpg" width="124" height="168" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/FranciscusXavier.jpg/186px-FranciscusXavier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/FranciscusXavier.jpg/248px-FranciscusXavier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="674" data-file-height="911" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Ignacio_de_Loyola" title="Ignacio de Loyola">Ignacio de Loyola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs" class="mw-redirect" title="Teresa de Jesús">Teresa de Jesús</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Javier" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Javier">Francisco Javier</a> prominent figures of <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A study made by the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Islamic_Communities_of_Spain" title="Union of Islamic Communities of Spain">Union of Islamic Communities of Spain</a> demonstrated that there were about 1,700,000 inhabitants of Muslim background living in Spain as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Spain&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, accounting for 3–4% of the total population of Spain. The vast majority was composed of immigrants and descendants originating from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and other African countries. More than 514,000 (30%) of them had Spanish nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>The recent waves of immigration have also led to an increasing number of <a href="/wiki/Hindus" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindus">Hindus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhists" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhists">Buddhists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sikhs">Sikhs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>. After the Reconquista in 1492, Muslims did not live in Spain for centuries. Late 19th-century colonial expansion in northwestern Africa gave a number of residents in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Morocco">Spanish Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> full citizenship. Their ranks have since been bolstered by recent immigration, especially from Morocco and Algeria.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> was practically non-existent in Spain from the 1492 expulsion until the 19th century, when Jews were again permitted to enter the country. Currently there are around 62,000 Jews in Spain, or 0.14% of the total population. Most are arrivals in the past century, while some are descendants of earlier Spanish Jews. Approximately 80,000 <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a> are thought to have lived in Spain prior to its expulsion.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Spain" title="Culture of Spain">Culture of Spain</a></div>
<p>Culturally, Spain is a <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western country</a>. Almost every aspect of Spanish life is permeated by its Roman heritage, making Spain one of the major <a href="/wiki/Romance-speaking_Europe" title="Romance-speaking Europe">Latin countries</a> of Europe. Spanish culture is marked by strong historic ties to Catholicism, which played a pivotal role in the country's formation and subsequent identity. Spanish art, architecture, cuisine, and music has been shaped by successive waves of foreign invaders, as well as by the country's Mediterranean climate and geography. The centuries-long colonial era globalised Spanish language and culture, with Spain also absorbing the cultural and commercial products of its diverse empire.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Heritage_Sites">World Heritage Sites</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites in Spain">World Heritage Sites in Spain</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Castles_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Castles in Spain">Castles in Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cathedrals_in_Spain" title="Cathedrals in Spain">Cathedrals in Spain</a></div>
<p>It should be noted that after <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (49) and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> (45), Spain is the third country in the world with the most <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>. At the present time it has 44 recognised sites, including the landscape of <a href="/wiki/Monte_Perdido" title="Monte Perdido">Monte Perdido</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>, which is shared with <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, the Prehistoric Rock Art Sites of the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4a_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Côa Valley">Côa Valley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siega_Verde" title="Siega Verde">Siega Verde</a>, which is shared with <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> (the Portuguese part being in the Côa Valley, <a href="/wiki/Guarda_District" title="Guarda District">Guarda</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Heritage_of_Mercury._Almad%C3%A9n_and_Idrija" title="Heritage of Mercury. Almadén and Idrija">Heritage of Mercury</a>, shared with <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[183]</a></sup> In addition, Spain has also 14 <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">Intangible cultural heritage</a>, or "Human treasures", Spain ranks first in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> according to <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_Lists" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage Lists">UNESCO's Intangible Cultural Heritage List</a>, tied with <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[184]</a></sup></p>
