<li>2009 — <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_Hercules" title="Tower of Hercules">Tower of Hercules</a> (A Coruña, Galicia).</li>
<li>2011 — <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Tramontana" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra de Tramontana">Cultural Landscape of the Serra de Tramuntana</a> (Majorca, Balearic Islands).</li>
<li>2012 — <a href="/wiki/Heritage_of_Mercury._Almad%C3%A9n_and_Idrija" title="Heritage of Mercury. Almadén and Idrija">Heritage of Mercury</a>. <a href="/wiki/Almad%C3%A9n" title="Almadén">Almadén</a> (Ciudad Real, Castile-La Mancha – Spanish part) and <a href="/wiki/Idrija" title="Idrija">Idrija</a> (Slovene Littoral – Slovenian part). (Shared with Slovenia).</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_literature" title="Spanish literature">Spanish literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Spanish Academy">Royal Spanish Academy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cervantes" title="Instituto Cervantes">Instituto Cervantes</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Basque_literature" title="Basque literature">Basque literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_literature" title="Catalan literature">Catalan literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Galician literature">Galician literature</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_literature" title="Latin American literature">Latin American literature</a></div>
<p>The earliest recorded examples of vernacular Romance-based literature date from the same time and location, the rich mix of Muslim, Jewish, and Christian cultures in Muslim Spain, in which Maimonides, Averroes, and others worked, the <a href="/wiki/Kharja" title="Kharja">Kharjas</a> (<i>Jarchas</i>).</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a>, the epic poem <i><a href="/wiki/Cantar_de_Mio_Cid" title="Cantar de Mio Cid">Cantar de Mio Cid</a></i> was written about a real man—his battles, conquests, and daily life.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg/170px-Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg/255px-Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg/340px-Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1237" data-file-height="1858" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bronze_statues_of_Don_Quixote_and_Sancho_Panza.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bronze statues of <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">Don Quixote</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sancho_Panza" title="Sancho Panza">Sancho Panza</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Madrid)" title="Plaza de España (Madrid)">Plaza de España</a> in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other major plays from the medieval times were <i><a href="/wiki/Mester_de_Juglar%C3%ADa" title="Mester de Juglaría">Mester de Juglaría</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mester_de_Clerec%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Mester de Clerecía">Mester de Clerecía</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Coplas_por_la_muerte_de_su_padre" class="mw-redirect" title="Coplas por la muerte de su padre">Coplas por la muerte de su padre</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Good_Love" title="The Book of Good Love">El Libro de buen amor</a></i> (The Book of Good Love).</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> the major plays are <i><a href="/wiki/La_Celestina" title="La Celestina">La Celestina</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/El_Lazarillo_de_Tormes" title="El Lazarillo de Tormes">El Lazarillo de Tormes</a></i>, while many religious literature was created with poets as <a href="/wiki/Luis_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Luis de León">Luis de León</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_la_Cruz" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan de la Cruz">San Juan de la Cruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Teresa_de_Jes%C3%BAs" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Teresa de Jesús">Santa Teresa de Jesús</a>, etc.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> is the most important period for Spanish culture. We are in the times of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>. The famous <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">Don Quijote de La Mancha</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a> was written in this time. Other writers from the period are: <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Quevedo" title="Francisco de Quevedo">Francisco de Quevedo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lope_de_Vega" title="Lope de Vega">Lope de Vega</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calder%C3%B3n_de_la_Barca" class="mw-redirect" title="Calderón de la Barca">Calderón de la Barca</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tirso_de_Molina" title="Tirso de Molina">Tirso de Molina</a>.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> we find names such as <a href="/wiki/Leandro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Morat%C3%ADn" title="Leandro Fernández de Moratín">Leandro Fernández de Moratín</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benito_Jer%C3%B3nimo_Feij%C3%B3o" class="mw-redirect" title="Benito Jerónimo Feijóo">Benito Jerónimo Feijóo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos" title="Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos">Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos</a> or <a href="/wiki/Leandro_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Morat%C3%ADn" title="Leandro Fernández de Moratín">Leandro Fernández de Moratín</a>.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romanticism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Zorrilla" title="José Zorrilla">José Zorrilla</a> created one of the most emblematic figures in European literature in <a href="/wiki/Don_Juan_Tenorio" title="Don Juan Tenorio">Don Juan Tenorio</a>. Other writers from this period are <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_Adolfo_B%C3%A9cquer" title="Gustavo Adolfo Bécquer">Gustavo Adolfo Bécquer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Espronceda" title="José de Espronceda">José de Espronceda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosal%C3%ADa_de_Castro" title="Rosalía de Castro">Rosalía de Castro</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Jos%C3%A9_de_Larra" title="Mariano José de Larra">Mariano José de Larra</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Realism_(arts)" title="Realism (arts)">Realism</a> we find names such as <a href="/wiki/Benito_P%C3%A9rez_Gald%C3%B3s" title="Benito Pérez Galdós">Benito Pérez Galdós</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emilia_Pardo_Baz%C3%A1n" title="Emilia Pardo Bazán">Emilia Pardo Bazán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Alas" title="Leopoldo Alas">Leopoldo Alas</a> (Clarín), <a href="/wiki/Concepci%C3%B3n_Arenal" title="Concepción Arenal">Concepción Arenal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Blasco_Ib%C3%A1%C3%B1ez" title="Vicente Blasco Ibáñez">Vicente Blasco Ibáñez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo" class="mw-redirect" title="Menéndez Pelayo">Menéndez Pelayo</a>. Realism offered depictions of contemporary life and society 'as they were'. In the spirit of general "Realism", Realist authors opted for depictions of everyday and banal activities and experiences, instead of romanticised or stylised presentations.</p>
<p>The group that has become known as the <a href="/wiki/Generation_of_1898" class="mw-redirect" title="Generation of 1898">Generation of 1898</a> was marked by the destruction of Spain's fleet in Cuba by US gunboats in 1898, which provoked a cultural crisis in Spain. The "Disaster" of 1898 led established writers to seek practical political, economic, and social solutions in essays grouped under the literary heading of <i>Regeneracionismo</i>. For a group of younger writers, among them <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Unamuno" title="Miguel de Unamuno">Miguel de Unamuno</a>, <a href="/wiki/P%C3%ADo_Baroja" title="Pío Baroja">Pío Baroja</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%ADnez_Ruiz" title="José Martínez Ruiz">José Martínez Ruiz</a> (Azorín), the Disaster and its cultural repercussions inspired a deeper, more radical literary shift that affected both form and content. These writers, along with <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_del_Valle-Incl%C3%A1n" title="Ramón del Valle-Inclán">Ramón del Valle-Inclán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Machado" title="Antonio Machado">Antonio Machado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramiro_de_Maeztu" title="Ramiro de Maeztu">Ramiro de Maeztu</a>, and Ángel Ganivet, came to be known as the Generation of '98.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:400px;max-width:400px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:131px;max-width:131px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Ram%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Valle_Incl%C3%A1n,_de_Audouard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ram%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Valle_Incl%C3%A1n%2C_de_Audouard.jpg/129px-Ram%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Valle_Incl%C3%A1n%2C_de_Audouard.jpg" width="129" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ram%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Valle_Incl%C3%A1n%2C_de_Audouard.jpg/194px-Ram%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Valle_Incl%C3%A1n%2C_de_Audouard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Ram%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Valle_Incl%C3%A1n%2C_de_Audouard.jpg/258px-Ram%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADa_del_Valle_Incl%C3%A1n%2C_de_Audouard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="418" data-file-height="438" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:137px;max-width:137px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Zambrano_late_years.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Zambrano_late_years.jpg/135px-Zambrano_late_years.jpg" width="135" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Zambrano_late_years.jpg/203px-Zambrano_late_years.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Zambrano_late_years.jpg/270px-Zambrano_late_years.jpg 2x" data-file-width="759" data-file-height="759" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:126px;max-width:126px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Lorca_(1914).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lorca_%281914%29.jpg/124px-Lorca_%281914%29.jpg" width="124" height="137" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lorca_%281914%29.jpg/186px-Lorca_%281914%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Lorca_%281914%29.jpg/248px-Lorca_%281914%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="545" data-file-height="600" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_del_Valle-Incl%C3%A1n" title="Ramón del Valle-Inclán">Ramón del Valle-Inclán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Zambrano" title="María Zambrano">María Zambrano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federico_Garc%C3%ADa_Lorca" title="Federico García Lorca">Federico García Lorca</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Generation of 1914 or <i>Novecentismo</i>. The next supposed "generation" of Spanish writers following those of '98 already calls into question the value of such terminology. By the year 1914—the year of the outbreak of the First World War and of the publication of the first major work of the generation's leading voice, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ortega_y_Gasset" title="José Ortega y Gasset">José Ortega y Gasset</a>—a number of slightly younger writers had established their own place within the Spanish cultural field.</p>
<p>Leading voices include the poet <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Juan Ramón Jiménez">Juan Ramón Jiménez</a>, the academics and essayists <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pidal" title="Ramón Menéndez Pidal">Ramón Menéndez Pidal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Mara%C3%B1%C3%B3n" title="Gregorio Marañón">Gregorio Marañón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Aza%C3%B1a" title="Manuel Azaña">Manuel Azaña</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Zambrano" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Zambrano">Maria Zambrano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eugeni_d%27Ors" title="Eugeni d'Ors">Eugeni d'Ors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clara_Campoamor" title="Clara Campoamor">Clara Campoamor</a> and Ortega y Gasset, and the novelists Gabriel Miró, <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_P%C3%A9rez_de_Ayala" title="Ramón Pérez de Ayala">Ramón Pérez de Ayala</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_G%C3%B3mez_de_la_Serna" title="Ramón Gómez de la Serna">Ramón Gómez de la Serna</a>. While still driven by the national and existential questions that obsessed the writers of '98, they approached these topics with a greater sense of distance and objectivity. <a href="/wiki/Salvador_de_Madariaga" title="Salvador de Madariaga">Salvador de Madariaga</a>, another prominent intellectual and writer, was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Europe" title="College of Europe">College of Europe</a> and the composer of the constitutive manifest of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_International" title="Liberal International">Liberal International</a>.</p>
<p>The Generation of 1927, where poets Pedro Salinas, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Guill%C3%A9n" title="Jorge Guillén">Jorge Guillén</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federico_Garc%C3%ADa_Lorca" title="Federico García Lorca">Federico García Lorca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Aleixandre" title="Vicente Aleixandre">Vicente Aleixandre</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1maso_Alonso" title="Dámaso Alonso">Dámaso Alonso</a>. All were scholars of their national literary heritage, again evidence of the impact of the calls of <i>regeneracionistas</i> and the Generation of 1898 for Spanish intelligence to turn at least partially inwards.</p>
<p>The two main writers in the second half of the 20th century were the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> laureate <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Jos%C3%A9_Cela" title="Camilo José Cela">Camilo José Cela</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Delibes" title="Miguel Delibes">Miguel Delibes</a> from <a href="/wiki/Generation_of_%2736" title="Generation of '36">Generation of '36</a>. Spain is one of the countries with the most number of laureates with the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>, and with <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin American</a> laureates they made the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish language</a> literature one of the most laureates of all. The Spanish writers are: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Echegaray" title="José Echegaray">José Echegaray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacinto_Benavente" title="Jacinto Benavente">Jacinto Benavente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Juan Ramón Jiménez">Juan Ramón Jiménez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Aleixandre" title="Vicente Aleixandre">Vicente Aleixandre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Jos%C3%A9_Cela" title="Camilo José Cela">Camilo José Cela</a>. The Portuguese writer <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Saramago" title="José Saramago">José Saramago</a>, also awarded with the prize, lived for many years in Spain and spoke both Portuguese and Spanish. He was also well known by his <a href="/wiki/Iberism" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberism">Iberist</a> ideas.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Generation_of_%2750" title="Generation of '50">Generation of '50</a> are also known as the children of the civil war. <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Chacel" title="Rosa Chacel">Rosa Chacel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Fuertes" title="Gloria Fuertes">Gloria Fuertes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Gil_de_Biedma" title="Jaime Gil de Biedma">Jaime Gil de Biedma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Goytisolo" title="Juan Goytisolo">Juan Goytisolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Mart%C3%ADn_Gaite" title="Carmen Martín Gaite">Carmen Martín Gaite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute" title="Ana María Matute">Ana María Matute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mars%C3%A9" title="Juan Marsé">Juan Marsé</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Blas_de_Otero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Blas de Otero (page does not exist)">Blas de Otero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Celaya" title="Gabriel Celaya">Gabriel Celaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Gamoneda" title="Antonio Gamoneda">Antonio Gamoneda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_S%C3%A1nchez_Ferlosio" title="Rafael Sánchez Ferlosio">Rafael Sánchez Ferlosio</a> or <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Aldecoa" title="Ignacio Aldecoa">Ignacio Aldecoa</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_art" title="Spanish art">Spanish art</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Meninas,_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez,_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Las_Meninas%2C_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/170px-Las_Meninas%2C_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" width="170" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Las_Meninas%2C_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/255px-Las_Meninas%2C_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Las_Meninas%2C_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg/340px-Las_Meninas%2C_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez%2C_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="26065" data-file-height="30000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Las_Meninas,_by_Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez,_from_Prado_in_Google_Earth.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Las_Meninas" title="Las Meninas">Las Meninas</a></i> (1656), <a href="/wiki/Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="Diego Velázquez">Diego Velázquez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museo_del_Prado" title="Museo del Prado">Museo del Prado</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Artists from Spain have been highly influential in the development of various European <a href="/wiki/Art_movement" title="Art movement">artistic movements</a>. Due to historical, geographical and generational diversity, Spanish art has known a great number of influences. The Moorish heritage in Spain, especially in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, is still evident today and European influences include Italy, Germany and France, especially during the <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">Neoclassical</a> periods.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age" title="Golden Age">Golden Age</a> we find painters such as <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">El Greco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Ribera" class="mw-redirect" title="José de Ribera">José de Ribera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Esteban_Murillo" title="Bartolomé Esteban Murillo">Bartolomé Esteban Murillo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Zurbar%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Zurbarán">Francisco Zurbarán</a>. Also inside Baroque period <a href="/wiki/Diego_Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="Diego Velázquez">Diego Velázquez</a> created some of the most famous Spanish portraits, like <a href="/wiki/Las_Meninas" title="Las Meninas">Las Meninas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Las_Hilanderas_(Vel%C3%A1zquez)" title="Las Hilanderas (Velázquez)">Las Hilanderas</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Goya" title="Francisco Goya">Francisco Goya</a> painted during a historical period that includes the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Spanish Independence War</a>, the fights between liberals and absolutists, and the raise of state-nations.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Sorolla" title="Joaquín Sorolla">Joaquín Sorolla</a> is a well-known impressionist painter and there are many important Spanish painters belonging to the modernism art movement, including <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD" title="Salvador Dalí">Salvador Dalí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Gris" title="Juan Gris">Juan Gris</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joan_Mir%C3%B3" title="Joan Miró">Joan Miró</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sculpture">Sculpture</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chillida-peine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Chillida-peine.jpg/220px-Chillida-peine.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Chillida-peine.jpg/330px-Chillida-peine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Chillida-peine.jpg/440px-Chillida-peine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="706" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chillida-peine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Comb of the Wind of <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Chillida" title="Eduardo Chillida">Eduardo Chillida</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Sebasti%C3%A1n" title="San Sebastián">San Sebastián</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Plateresque style extended from beginnings of the 16th century until the last third of the century and its stylistic influence pervaded the works of all great Spanish artists of the time. <a href="/wiki/Alonso_Berruguete" title="Alonso Berruguete">Alonso Berruguete</a> (<a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">Valladolid</a> School) is called the "Prince of Spanish sculpture". His main works were the upper stalls of the choir of the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Toledo" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of Toledo">Cathedral of Toledo</a>, the tomb of Cardinal Tavera in the same Cathedral, and the altarpiece of the Visitation in the church of Santa Úrsula in the same locality. Other notable sculptors were <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Ord%C3%B3%C3%B1ez" title="Bartolomé Ordóñez">Bartolomé Ordóñez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Silo%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Diego de Siloé">Diego de Siloé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Juni" title="Juan de Juni">Juan de Juni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dami%C3%A0_Forment" title="Damià Forment">Damián Forment</a>.</p>
<p>There were two Schools of special flair and talent: the <a href="/wiki/Sevillian_school_of_sculpture" title="Sevillian school of sculpture">Seville School</a>, to which <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mart%C3%ADnez_Monta%C3%B1%C3%A9s" title="Juan Martínez Montañés">Juan Martínez Montañés</a> belonged, whose most celebrated works are the Crucifix in the Cathedral of Seville, another in Vergara, and a Saint John; and the <a href="/wiki/Granadan_school_of_sculpture" title="Granadan school of sculpture">Granada School</a>, to which <a href="/wiki/Alonso_Cano" class="mw-redirect" title="Alonso Cano">Alonso Cano</a> belonged, to whom an Immaculate Conception and a Virgin of Rosary, are attributed.</p>
<p>Other notable Andalusian Baroque sculptors were <a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_Mena" title="Pedro de Mena">Pedro de Mena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Rold%C3%A1n" title="Pedro Roldán">Pedro Roldán</a> and his daughter <a href="/wiki/Luisa_Rold%C3%A1n" title="Luisa Roldán">Luisa Roldán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Mesa" title="Juan de Mesa">Juan de Mesa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Duque_Cornejo" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro Duque Cornejo">Pedro Duque Cornejo</a>. In the 20th century the most important Spanish sculptors were <a href="/wiki/Julio_Gonz%C3%A1lez_(sculptor)" title="Julio González (sculptor)">Julio González</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Gargallo" title="Pablo Gargallo">Pablo Gargallo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Chillida" title="Eduardo Chillida">Eduardo Chillida</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Serrano" title="Pablo Serrano">Pablo Serrano</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Spain" title="Cinema of Spain">Cinema of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg/170px-Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg/255px-Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg/340px-Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="774" data-file-height="1068" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pedro_Almodovar_and_Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Pedro_Almod%C3%B3var" title="Pedro Almodóvar">Pedro Almodóvar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz" title="Penélope Cruz">Penélope Cruz</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Princess_of_Asturias_Awards" title="Princess of Asturias Awards">Princess of Asturias Awards</a>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spanish cinema has achieved major international success including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Oscars</a> for recent films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Pan%27s_Labyrinth" title="Pan's Labyrinth">Pan's Labyrinth</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Volver" title="Volver">Volver</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[185]</a></sup> In the long history of Spanish cinema, the great filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bu%C3%B1uel" title="Luis Buñuel">Luis Buñuel</a> was the first to achieve world recognition, followed by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Almod%C3%B3var" title="Pedro Almodóvar">Pedro Almodóvar</a> in the 1980s (<a href="/wiki/La_Movida_Madrile%C3%B1a" title="La Movida Madrileña">La Movida Madrileña</a>). <a href="/wiki/Mario_Camus" title="Mario Camus">Mario Camus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pilar_Mir%C3%B3" title="Pilar Miró">Pilar Miró</a> worked together in <a href="/wiki/Curro_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Curro Jiménez">Curro Jiménez</a>.</p>
<p>Spanish cinema has also seen international success over the years with films by <a href="/wiki/Film_director" title="Film director">directors</a> like <a href="/wiki/Segundo_de_Chom%C3%B3n" title="Segundo de Chomón">Segundo de Chomón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flori%C3%A1n_Rey" title="Florián Rey">Florián Rey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Garc%C3%ADa_Berlanga" title="Luis García Berlanga">Luis García Berlanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Saura" title="Carlos Saura">Carlos Saura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julio_Medem" title="Julio Medem">Julio Medem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Coixet" title="Isabel Coixet">Isabel Coixet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Amen%C3%A1bar" title="Alejandro Amenábar">Alejandro Amenábar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ic%C3%ADar_Bolla%C3%ADn" title="Icíar Bollaín">Icíar Bollaín</a> and brothers <a href="/wiki/David_Trueba" title="David Trueba">David Trueba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Trueba" title="Fernando Trueba">Fernando Trueba</a>.</p>
<p>Actresses <a href="/wiki/Sara_Montiel" title="Sara Montiel">Sara Montiel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pen%C3%A9lope_Cruz" title="Penélope Cruz">Penélope Cruz</a> or actor <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Banderas" title="Antonio Banderas">Antonio Banderas</a> are among those who have become <a href="/wiki/Cinema_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Cinema in the United States">Hollywood</a> stars.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_architecture" title="Spanish architecture">Spanish architecture</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg/170px-Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg/255px-Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg/340px-Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sagrada_Familia_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a href="/wiki/Sagrada_Fam%C3%ADlia" title="Sagrada Família">Sagrada Família</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Antoni_Gaud%C3%AD" title="Antoni Gaudí">Antoni Gaudí</a>, Barcelona</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Due to its historical and geographical diversity, Spanish architecture has drawn from a host of influences. An important provincial city founded by the Romans and with an extensive <a href="/wiki/Roman_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman era">Roman era</a> infrastructure, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Córdoba, Spain">Córdoba</a> became the cultural capital, including fine Arabic style architecture, during the time of the Islamic <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Umayyad dynasty">Umayyad dynasty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[186]</a></sup> Later Arab style architecture continued to be developed under successive Islamic dynasties, ending with the <a href="/wiki/Nasrid_dynasty" title="Nasrid dynasty">Nasrid</a>, which built its famed palace complex in <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>.</p>
<p>Simultaneously, the Christian kingdoms gradually emerged and developed their own styles; developing a <a href="/wiki/Pre-Romanesque" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Romanesque">pre-Romanesque</a> style when for a while isolated from contemporary mainstream European architectural influences during the earlier Middle Ages, they later integrated the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> streams. There was then an extraordinary flowering of the Gothic style that resulted in numerous instances being built throughout the entire territory. The <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">Mudéjar</a> style, from the 12th to 17th centuries, was developed by introducing Arab style motifs, patterns and elements into European architecture.</p>
<p>The arrival of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">Modernism</a> in the academic arena produced much of the architecture of the 20th century. An influential style centred in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Modernisme" title="Modernisme">modernisme</a>, produced a number of important architects, of which <a href="/wiki/Gaud%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaudí">Gaudí</a> is one. The <a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">International style</a> was led by groups like <a href="/wiki/GATEPAC" title="GATEPAC">GATEPAC</a>. Spain is currently experiencing a revolution in <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_architecture" title="Contemporary architecture">contemporary architecture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Category:Spanish_architects" title="Category:Spanish architects">Spanish architects</a> like <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Moneo" title="Rafael Moneo">Rafael Moneo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Bofill" title="Ricardo Bofill">Ricardo Bofill</a> as well as many others have gained worldwide renown.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Spain" title="Music of Spain">Music of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Belen_maya.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Belen_maya.jpg/170px-Belen_maya.jpg" width="170" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Belen_maya.jpg/255px-Belen_maya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Belen_maya.jpg/340px-Belen_maya.jpg 2x" data-file-width="376" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Belen_maya.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">Flamenco</a> is an Andalusian artistic form that evolved from the <a href="/wiki/Seguidilla" title="Seguidilla">Seguidilla</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spanish music is often considered abroad to be synonymous with <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">flamenco</a>, a West Andalusian musical genre, which, contrary to popular belief, is not widespread outside that region. Various regional styles of <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> abound in Aragon, Catalonia, Valencia, Castile, the Basque Country, Galicia, Cantabria and Asturias. Pop, rock, hip hop and heavy metal are also popular.</p>
<p>In the field of <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a>, Spain has produced a number of noted <a href="/wiki/Composers" class="mw-redirect" title="Composers">composers</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Alb%C3%A9niz" title="Isaac Albéniz">Isaac Albéniz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Falla" title="Manuel de Falla">Manuel de Falla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Granados" title="Enrique Granados">Enrique Granados</a> and singers and performers such as <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Domingo" title="Plácido Domingo">Plácido Domingo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Carreras" title="José Carreras">José Carreras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Caball%C3%A9" title="Montserrat Caballé">Montserrat Caballé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alicia_de_Larrocha" title="Alicia de Larrocha">Alicia de Larrocha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Kraus" title="Alfredo Kraus">Alfredo Kraus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Casals" title="Pablo Casals">Pablo Casals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Vi%C3%B1es" title="Ricardo Viñes">Ricardo Viñes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Iturbi" title="José Iturbi">José Iturbi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_de_Sarasate" title="Pablo de Sarasate">Pablo de Sarasate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Savall" title="Jordi Savall">Jordi Savall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Teresa_Berganza" title="Teresa Berganza">Teresa Berganza</a>. In Spain there are over forty professional orchestras, including the <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_Symphony_and_Catalonia_National_Orchestra" title="Barcelona Symphony and Catalonia National Orchestra">Orquestra Simfònica de Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orquesta_Nacional_de_Espa%C3%B1a" class="mw-redirect" title="Orquesta Nacional de España">Orquesta Nacional de España</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Orquesta_Sinf%C3%B3nica_de_Madrid" title="Orquesta Sinfónica de Madrid">Orquesta Sinfónica de Madrid</a>. Major <a href="/wiki/Opera_houses" class="mw-redirect" title="Opera houses">opera houses</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Real" title="Teatro Real">Teatro Real</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Teatre_del_Liceu" class="mw-redirect" title="Gran Teatre del Liceu">Gran Teatre del Liceu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Arriaga" title="Teatro Arriaga">Teatro Arriaga</a> and the <a href="/wiki/El_Palau_de_les_Arts_Reina_Sof%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="El Palau de les Arts Reina Sofía">El Palau de les Arts Reina Sofía</a>.</p>
<p>Thousands of music fans also travel to Spain each year for internationally recognised summer music festivals <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B3nar" title="Sónar">Sónar</a> which often features the top up and coming pop and techno acts, and <a href="/wiki/Festival_Internacional_de_Benic%C3%A0ssim" title="Festival Internacional de Benicàssim">Benicàssim</a> which tends to feature alternative rock and dance acts.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[187]</a></sup> Both festivals mark Spain as an international music presence and reflect the tastes of young people in the country.</p>
<p>The most popular traditional <a href="/wiki/Musical_instrument" title="Musical instrument">musical instrument</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guitar" title="Guitar">guitar</a>, originated in Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[188]</a></sup> Typical of the north are the traditional bag pipers or <i><a href="/wiki/Gaita_(bagpipe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaita (bagpipe)">gaiteros</a></i>, mainly in Asturias and Galicia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine" title="Spanish cuisine">Spanish cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg/220px-Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg/330px-Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg/440px-Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2427" data-file-height="1763" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paella_de_marisco_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">Paella</a>, a traditional <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian</a> dish<sup id="cite_ref-paella_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paella-201">[189]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Spanish cuisine consists of a great variety of dishes which stem from differences in geography, culture and climate. It is heavily influenced by seafood available from the waters that surround the country, and reflects the country's deep <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> roots. Spain's extensive history with many cultural influences has led to a unique cuisine. In particular, three main divisions are easily identified:</p>
<p><i><b>Mediterranean</b></i> Spain – all such coastal regions, from Catalonia to Andalusia – heavy use of seafood, such as <i>pescaíto frito</i> (fried fish); several cold soups like <i><a href="/wiki/Gazpacho" title="Gazpacho">gazpacho</a></i>; and many rice-based dishes like <i><a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">paella</a></i> from Valencia<sup id="cite_ref-paella_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paella-201">[189]</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Arr%C3%B2s_negre" title="Arròs negre">arròs negre</a></i> (black rice) from Catalonia.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><b>Inner</b></i> Spain – Castile – hot, thick soups such as the bread and garlic-based <i>Castilian soup</i>, along with substantious stews such as <i><a href="/wiki/Cocido_madrile%C3%B1o" title="Cocido madrileño">cocido madrileño</a></i>. Food is traditionally conserved by salting, like <a href="/wiki/Spanish_ham" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish ham">Spanish ham</a>, or immersed in <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, like <a href="/wiki/Manchego_cheese" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchego cheese">Manchego cheese</a>.</p>
<p><i><b>Atlantic</b></i> Spain – the whole Northern coast, including <a href="/wiki/Asturian_cuisine" title="Asturian cuisine">Asturian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basque_cuisine" title="Basque cuisine">Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_cuisine" title="Cantabrian cuisine">Cantabrian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galician_cuisine" title="Galician cuisine">Galician cuisine</a> – vegetable and fish-based stews like <i><a href="/wiki/Caldo_gallego" title="Caldo gallego">caldo gallego</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Marmitako" class="mw-redirect" title="Marmitako">marmitako</a></i>. Also, the lightly cured <i><a href="/wiki/Lac%C3%B3n_Gallego" title="Lacón Gallego">lacón</a></i> ham. The best known cuisine of the northern countries often rely on ocean seafood, like the Basque-style <a href="/wiki/Cod" title="Cod">cod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albacore" title="Albacore">albacore</a> or <a href="/wiki/Anchovy" title="Anchovy">anchovy</a> or the Galician octopus-based <i><a href="/wiki/Polbo_%C3%A1_feira" title="Polbo á feira">polbo á feira</a></i> and shellfish dishes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Spain" title="Sport in Spain">Sport in Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg/170px-Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg/255px-Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg/340px-Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barcelona-1992-rr-800.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While varieties of football had been played in Spain as far back as Roman times, sport in Spain has been dominated by English style <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> since the early 20th century. <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid C.F.</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> are two of the most successful football clubs in the world. <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">The country's national football team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA European Football Championship">UEFA European Football Championship</a> in 1964, 2008 and 2012 and the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010</a>, and is the first team to ever win three back-to-back major international tournaments.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorcycling" title="Motorcycling">motorcycling</a> and, lately, <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> are also important due to the presence of Spanish champions in all these disciplines. Today, Spain is a major world sports powerhouse, especially since the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> that were hosted in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, which stimulated a great deal of interest in sports in the country. The tourism industry has led to an improvement in sports infrastructure, especially for <a href="/wiki/Water_sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Water sports">water sports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rafael_Nadal" title="Rafael Nadal">Rafael Nadal</a> is the leading Spanish tennis player and has won several Grand Slam titles including the Wimbledon 2010 men's singles. In north Spain, the game of <a href="/wiki/Basque_pelota" title="Basque pelota">pelota</a> is very popular. <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Contador" title="Alberto Contador">Alberto Contador</a> is the leading Spanish cyclist and has won several Grand Tour titles including two <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a> titles.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_holidays_and_festivals">Public holidays and festivals</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Spain" title="Public holidays in Spain">Public holidays in Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_of_International_Tourist_Interest_of_Spain" title="Fiestas of International Tourist Interest of Spain">Fiestas of International Tourist Interest of Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_of_National_Tourist_Interest_of_Spain" title="Fiestas of National Tourist Interest of Spain">Fiestas of National Tourist Interest of Spain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg/170px-Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg/255px-Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg/340px-Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sanfermines_Vaquillas_Pamplona_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/San_Ferm%C3%ADn" title="San Fermín">San Fermín</a> festival, <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Public holidays celebrated in Spain include a mix of religious (<a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>), national and regional observances. Each municipality is allowed to declare a maximum of 14 <a href="/wiki/Public_holiday" title="Public holiday">public holidays</a> per year; up to nine of these are chosen by the national government and at least two are chosen locally.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[191]</a></sup> Spain's National Day (<i><a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Nacional_de_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Fiesta Nacional de España">Fiesta Nacional de España</a></i>) is 12 October, the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Discovery of America">Discovery of America</a> and commemorate <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Pillar" title="Our Lady of the Pillar">Our Lady of the Pillar</a> feast, patroness of <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a> and throughout Spain.</p>
<p>There are many festivals and festivities in Spain. Some of them are known worldwide, and every year millions of people from all over the world go to Spain to experience one of these festivals. One of the most famous is <a href="/wiki/San_Ferm%C3%ADn" title="San Fermín">San Fermín</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Pamplona" title="Pamplona">Pamplona</a>. While its most famous event is the <i>encierro</i>, or the <a href="/wiki/Running_of_the_bulls" class="mw-redirect" title="Running of the bulls">running of the bulls</a>, which happens at 8:00 am from 7 to 14 July, the week-long celebration involves many other traditional and folkloric events. Its events were central to the plot of The Sun Also Rises, by <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Hemingway" title="Ernest Hemingway">Ernest Hemingway</a>, which brought it to the general attention of English-speaking people. As a result, it has become one of the most internationally renowned fiestas in Spain, with over 1,000,000 people attending every year.</p>
<p>Other festivals include the carnivals in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">Holy Week</a> in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">Castile and León</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-a-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-a_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-a_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The Spanish Constitution does not establish any official name for Spain, even though the terms <i>España</i> (Spain), <i>Estado español</i> (Spanish State) and <i>Nación española</i> (Spanish Nation) are used throughout the document. Nonetheless, the Spanish Ministry of Foreign Affairs established in an ordinance published in 1984 that the denominations <i>España</i> (Spain) and <i>Reino de España</i> (Kingdom of Spain) are equally valid to designate Spain in international treaties. This term, Kingdom of Spain, is widely used by the government in national and international affairs of all kinds, including foreign treaties as well as national official documents, and is therefore recognised as the official name by many international organisations.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-b-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-b_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-b_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">In Spain, <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Spain" title="Languages of Spain">other languages</a> have been officially recognised as legitimate <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_language" title="Indigenous language">autochthonous</a> <a href="/wiki/Regional_language" title="Regional language">(regional) languages</a> under the <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a>. In each of these, Spain's official name (Spanish: <span lang="es"><i>Reino de España</i></span>, pronounced: <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[ˈreino ð(e) esˈpaɲa]</a></span>) is as follows:</span>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">Aragonese</a>: <span lang="an"><i>Reino d’Espanya</i></span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ˈreino ðesˈpaɲa]</a></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a>: <span lang="ast"><i>Reinu d’España</i></span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Astur-Leonese" title="Help:IPA for Astur-Leonese">[ˈreinu ðesˈpaɲa]</a></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>: <span lang="eu"><i>Espainiako Erresuma</i></span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Basque" title="Help:IPA for Basque">[es̺paɲiako eres̺uma]</a></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>: <span lang="ca"><i>Regne d’Espanya</i></span>, <span class="nowrap"><small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Catalan" title="Help:IPA for Catalan">[ˈreŋnə ðəsˈpaɲə]</a></span></span>
<ul>
<li><small>Valencian:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Catalan" title="Help:IPA for Catalan">[ˈreŋne ðesˈpaɲa]</a></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>: <span lang="gl"><i>Reino de España</i></span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Galician" title="Help:IPA for Galician">[ˈreino ð(e) esˈpaɲa]</a></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>: <span lang="oc"><i>Reiaume d’Espanha</i></span>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Occitan" title="Help:IPA for Occitan">[reˈjawme ðesˈpaɲɔ]</a></span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-c-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-c_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-c_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The official Spanish language of the State is established in the Section 3 of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a> to be Castilian.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[3]</a></sup> In some <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous communities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> are co-official languages. <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">Aragonese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a> (locally known as <a href="/wiki/Aranese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Aranese language">Aranese</a>) have some degree of official recognition.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) since 1993.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As of July 2015, Spain's population was 46,439,864. In the same month the number of citizens with Spanish citizenship reached 41,996,253. The number of foreigners (i.e. immigrants, ex-pats and refugees) permanently living in Spain was estimated to be at 4,426,811 (9.54%) in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[6]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_peseta" title="Spanish peseta">Peseta</a> before 2002.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-e-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-e_16-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as it is shared with other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states. Also, the <a href="/wiki/.cat" title=".cat">.cat</a> domain is used in <a href="/wiki/Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans" class="mw-redirect" title="Països Catalans">Catalan-speaking territories</a>, <a href="/wiki/.gal" title=".gal">.gal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Galiza" class="mw-redirect" title="Galiza">Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/.eus" title=".eus">.eus</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Euskal_Herria" class="mw-redirect" title="Euskal Herria">Basque-speaking area</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">list of transcontinental countries</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i><a href="/wiki/Latifundia" class="mw-redirect" title="Latifundia">latifundia</a></i> (sing., <i>latifundium</i>), large estates controlled by the aristocracy, were superimposed on the existing Iberian landholding system.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The poets <a href="/wiki/Martial" title="Martial">Martial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quintilian" title="Quintilian">Quintilian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lucan" title="Lucan">Lucan</a> were also born in Hispania.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-38">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Berbers soon gave up attempting to settle the harsh lands in the north of the <a href="/wiki/Meseta_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="Meseta Central">Meseta Central</a> (Inner Plateau) handed to them by the Arab rulers.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-48">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For the related expulsions that followed see <a href="/wiki/Morisco" title="Morisco">Morisco</a>.</span></li>

<hr />
<p><span style="text-align:left; font-size:85%">1. All twenty-eight member states of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> are also members of the WTO in their own right:</span></p>
<ul>
<li><span style="text-align:left; font-size:85%"><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Austria" title="Economy of Austria">Austria</a></span></li>

<li><span style="text-align:left; font-size:85%"><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Croatia" title="Economy of Croatia">Croatia</a></span></li>
<li><span style="text-align:left; font-size:85%"><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cyprus" title="Economy of Cyprus">Cyprus</a></span></li>
<li><span style="text-align:left; font-size:85%"><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Economy of the Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a></span></li>
<li><span style="text-align:left; font-size:85%"><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Denmark" title="Economy of Denmark">Denmark</a></span></li>

<p><span style="text-align:left; font-size:85%"><br />
2. <a href="/wiki/Special_administrative_regions_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Special administrative regions of the People's Republic of China">Special administrative regions of the People's Republic of China</a>, participates as "Hong Kong, China" and "Macao China".<br />
3. Officially the Republic of China, participates as "<a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">Separate Customs Territory of Taiwan, Penghu, Kinmen and Matsu</a>", and "Chinese Taipei" in short.</span></p>
